Japanese Government Plans to Reform Administrative Institutions; Starting With Reforming the Cabinet System 65

(Nanjing) After the end of the special parliament in May, Prime Minister Hirota will reform the administrative institutions, which is the first step in the popular administration reform advocated by the current cabinet. On the one hand, the Cabinet Investigation Bureau and the Legislative Bureau, according to their previous decisions, believe that the following two points should be emphasized as fundamental guidelines when reforming administrative institutions: 1. Reforming the cabinet system and the parliamentary system to correct the current political institutions. 2. Fundamental renovation of personnel administration. However, the government is currently advocating starting with reforming the cabinet system, so the director of the Yoshida Cabinet Investigation Bureau will make important proposals to Prime Minister Hirota within days, and its trend is extremely worthy of attention. The three points advocated by the Investigation Bureau are as follows:

Reform of the Cabinet System

The cabinet meeting, which decides the pivot of national affairs, is currently composed of the Prime Minister and the thirteen Ministers of State, but it has lost the function of a collegial body for conducting sincere consultations and agreements. There is a risk that the cabinet meeting will fall into a formal meeting and there is no possibility of sincere consultations. In fact, it is extremely difficult to discuss matters from top to bottom. This is evident from the need to hold five-minister meetings and internal affairs cabinet member meetings in the past. Since the cabinet has thirteen Ministers of State, it cannot be discussed and decided once an opposing view arises. In other words, important issues are actually decided by the Prime Minister or two or three cabinet members, and there are few cases where the cabinet meeting fully discusses them. Therefore, in order to truly strengthen the cabinet and clarify responsible politics, the function of the cabinet meeting as a collegial body must be brought to the maximum extent. Therefore, the number of Ministers of State must first be limited to six or seven, and all of them must be ministers without portfolio, and each province will have a separate chief. In this way, in addition to the fact that the cabinet meeting can actually decide national policies at the center and effectively strengthen the cabinet, ministers of state can often seek smooth will between each other and can fully develop discussions on national policies.

Renovation of Personnel Administration

A personnel bureau is established in the cabinet to be responsible for the appointment and dismissal of officials in various provinces, except for the army, navy, and judiciary. When officials in various provinces are transferred, the abuse of changing positions due to promotion must be corrected. Specialists must be cultivated in the vertical system. When transferring, it should be limited to within one province. If it is a related matter, in order to seek personal integration between various provinces, it can be carried out between the relevant provinces. The above-mentioned changes, such as transportation relations, can be mutually transferred between the Civil Engineering Bureau of the Ministry of Internal Affairs, the various bureaus of the Railway Ministry, and the Management Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, and commercial trade relations can be carried out between the Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Commerce and Industry. The Commerce Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the various customs offices of the Ministry of Finance, etc., are sufficient to form an organic personal relationship and can also be used to provide comprehensive training for officials in various administrative departments. (Dentsu Telegram, 23rd)

Austria's Conscription System to Be Implemented This Autumn 66

Vienna The conscription system unanimously passed by the Austrian Parliament on April 1 will be implemented this autumn. The government newspaper today disclosed this decision and said that men born in 1915 must be called up for physical examination in June. According to this conscription system, in the event of an emergency, all strong men between the ages of eighteen and forty-five have the obligation to enlist in the army. The Little Entente countries have protested against this conscription system because it violates the Treaty of Saint-Germain. An Austrian newspaper published an official statement in response, saying that this law is not compulsory military service, but only labor service, so it does not conflict with the treaty. The Treaty of Saint-Germain abolishes the Austrian compulsory military service system and limits the Austrian army to 30,000 men. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation Requests Relief; Ministry of Industry Replied 71

(Nanjing) The Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation, led by Lu Xingzhuang, previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, stating that 200 million yuan of the Reconstruction Public Bonds should be allocated to provide mortgage loans for national goods manufacturers, and that industrial control laws and regulations should be promulgated and strictly enforced. The two ministries have repeatedly consulted and submitted the matter to the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Examination Committee for handling. The Ministry of Industry approved the submission, stating that the issuance of Reconstruction Public Bonds relates to the country's overall plan, and its use and distribution should be handled in a unified manner. The request to implement factory mortgage loans will be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. As for the industrial control measures, the Ministry is carefully discussing them, and will implement them as soon as a plan is formulated and submitted for approval. Furthermore, the Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation has not been approved for registration in accordance with the registration rules for agricultural, industrial, and mining groups. Please follow the rules and submit a request for registration. The Ministry of Industry consulted the Ministry of Finance, requesting consideration of factory loans. The Ministry of Finance replied, stating that it had previously received a request from the Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation to approve the allocation of 200 million yuan of the Reconstruction Public Bonds to the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications for the exclusive management of mortgage loans for national goods factories. The Ministry has always attached great importance to rescuing industry and commerce. Last year, the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Examination Committee was established to handle industrial and commercial loans. The Ministry allocated 20 million yuan of Treasury Bills as the second guarantee for the loans to rescue Shanghai's industry and commerce. The ten principles for issuing loans clearly stipulate that loan applications from industry and commerce are limited to factories that manufacture national goods, businesses that sell national goods, and those who transport national goods for export. The Loan Committee was ordered to comply with this, and the Shanghai Banking Association and the Chamber of Commerce were notified accordingly. If the factories of the Association do need loans to relieve them, they should contact them directly in accordance with the loan details regulations approved and approved by the Loan Committee. The reply was in accordance with the previous advice. (Special Telegram, 23rd)

The Food of the Ancient Peking Man at Zhoukoudian (Part 2) 98

— Original by Dr. Ralph W. Chaney, Translated by Chen Shaoyan

Scholars have discussed this before. They all believe that these beasts would only gnaw a small hole at the hard end of the nuts and would never chew the entire nut into fragments, just like squirrels do with walnuts and other nuts. At the experimental station of the University of California, dried hackberry fruits were fed to rodents kept in cages, but the results showed that they did not particularly like this type of food and were not accustomed to it, because they never chewed into the inside when eating the hard nuts provided.

The behavior of monkeys kept in cages is even more significant. They quickly accepted these dried fruits and chewed them all into pieces, swallowing the pulp and nut fragments together. However, everyone knows that there were no monkeys living in northern China during the Ice Age. Therefore, the fragments of hard nuts accumulated in the cave should be remnants of food discarded by the ancient cave dwellers, and can be considered garbage, rather than being left behind by rodents.

From this perspective, this can be regarded as the earliest record of humans using plants as food in prehistoric times. In such a cold and dry place, fresh fruits and nuts were rare. We can assume that the "Peking Man" at that time gathered these hackberry fruits from the bushes near his home and crushed them to supplement his meals, just like the natives of the southwestern United States do today. This is the best explanation for the large accumulation of hard nut fragments in the cave.

The cranial capacity of the "Peking Man" skull clearly shows that this early human was able to speak. In our imagination, we seem to be able to hear the "Peking Woman" calling out to the "Peking Child" to eat hackberry pudding in that language that disappeared millions of years ago.

As I was about to leave this cave on a small mountain in northern China, which was the home of ancient humans a million years ago, my Chinese companions kindly gave me the opportunity to choose a piece of breccia from the cave to take away. At that time, I picked up a piece from a pile of materials I had excavated from the cave, which weighed about two pounds. This stone revealed many fragments of burned bones and a large fragment of quartz. Because one end of the stone was uneven and needed to be repaired, I chiseled it off with my hammer. How surprised I was to see that the cross-section of this breccia was almost entirely hackberry kernels!

Although this is just a stone, it contains not only the remnants of food from before human history, including both meat and plants, but also crude stone tools. These tools were used by the "Peking Man" to kill bison, cut fresh meat, and crush the hackberry fruits. These deposits in the caves tell us everything about the dietary habits of ancient humans before humans recorded the details of their lives in writing.

Accumulation of hackberry shell fragments in the cave

Page 8

Japan's Southern Advance Policy Establishes the Taiwan Colonization Company to Develop Industries in Taiwan, South China, and Southeast Asia, as an Economic Organization for Implementing the Southern Advance 99

Xiamen Dispatch: Japan has recently been loudly advocating "Northern Defense, Southern Advance." As a result, the Southern Advance policy has become extremely active. Originally, after the joint conference of naval and military departments outside of South China consuls and the army, and the tropical industry conference held last year, the policy toward the south has been very aggressive. After the Hirota cabinet was established, the Governor of Taiwan, Nakagawa, went to Tokyo and proposed the "Establishment of the Taiwan Colonization Company." He obtained Hirota's approval. Recently, the cabinet decided to submit it to the parliament. Most of it can pass the outline of the Colonization Company Act.

* Name: Taiwan Colonization Co., Ltd.

* Purpose: To develop Taiwan, South China, and Southeast Asia and promote the development of their industries. Also, to make investments for the same purpose.

* Capital: 30 million yuan, with an annual amount of 15 million yuan. The government will contribute in kind, and the majority of the remaining annual amount will be contributed by sugar manufacturing companies.

* Executives: One president and one vice president, three directors, and two supervisors, all appointed by the government, responsible for business operations.

After the Taiwan Governor's Office received the news that the case had been discussed and resolved by the cabinet, the office was very tense. Government official Hiratsuka summoned Internal Affairs Bureau Chief Obana, Industry Bureau Chief Ichinose, Finance Bureau Chief Eto, and other relevant officials to the Governor's Office at 10:00 AM on the 16th to hold a consultation meeting on the establishment of the Colonization Company. It was decided that the heads of relevant departments would each produce specific investigation plans. At 9:00 AM on the 18th, Hiratsuka again summoned Foreign Affairs Section Chief Sakamoto, Investigation Section Chief Haraguchi, Finance Section Chief Yamagishi, and Industry and Commerce Section Chief Suda to discuss in detail the facilities fees for South China and Southeast Asia. The Governor's Office also, taking the development of the Southern Advance as a standpoint, has an annual facility fee budget of nearly 600,000 yuan for the development or expansion of Japanese businesses in South China and Southeast Asia. In Showa 11 (1936), 35,000 yuan was added, making it 617,862 yuan. After the two meetings, Hiratsuka is scheduled to go to Tokyo on the 22nd to meet with Hirota to discuss the Colonization Company plan, so that its implementation can be actively realized. In addition, Suda, Chief of the Industry and Commerce Section, who was specially dispatched by the Governor's Office to inspect industries and commerce in Southeast Asia, returned to Taiwan on the 16th and issued a statement, saying: "Since the Philippines' independence, its relationship with Japan, especially Taiwan, has greatly improved. In the future, there will be great cooperation in the economic field. The economic downturn in the Philippines and the Dutch East Indies is very severe, due to the large decrease in sugar production and the fall in rice prices. The British Malayan Peninsula and Singapore are better. In Siam, I met with Mr. Yasukawa and his economic inspection group, and we discussed major activities to cooperate economically with various parties. Since the Siamese revolution, the pro-British policy has changed to a pro-Japanese policy. Recently, the Yokohama Specie Bank will open a branch in Siam, and future development is greatly expected. However, since the products of Taiwan and Southeast Asia are roughly the same, Taiwan's special products must be heavily promoted. Raw materials can be taken from Southeast Asia, then processed in Taiwan, making it industrialized. This is a major fundamental strategy."

On the military front, the Japanese side is strengthening the Magong naval port in Penghu (recently, due to foreign ships repeatedly entering the Magong fortress, the Japanese side believes there is espionage suspicion and has specifically sealed off Magong Port from July 1st, prohibiting foreign ships from entering), and developing aviation. Regular flights between Fukuoka, Japan, and Taipei, Taiwan, have already been launched and will be extended from Taiwan to Bangkok, the capital of Siam, to compete with British aviation between Singapore and Hong Kong. Furthermore, the Japanese government decided to unify the Southern Advance policy and plans to abolish the South Seas Bureau, which is responsible for governing the mandated territory of the South Seas (Caroline) Islands, and make it subordinate to the Governor of Taiwan. Under the Taiwan Governor's Office, a South Seas Bureau would be established to govern it. The army and navy strongly advocate this proposal. The Ministry of Colonial Affairs believes that if such a policy is adopted, the mandated territory will be completely transformed into a colony, which may cause international repercussions. They are still considering it and have not yet implemented it. (April 23rd)

From the numbers listed above, it can be seen that Shilon handled the largest amount of exports, followed by Mitsubishi and Li Feng. Kong Xiangrong Arrives in Jinan to Discuss Key Strategies for Harnessing the Yellow River; Plans to Dredge the Lower Reaches of the Yellow River; Han Asks for a Railway to Be Built Along the Banks 101

Jinan Dispatch: Kong Xiangrong, Acting Chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission and Chief Organizer of the Dongzhuang Yellow River Closure Project in Shandong, after the completion of the closure of the breach, went to Beijing and Shanghai to report to the central authorities on the closure situation and to discuss future river defense issues. After finishing his business in Beijing, he took the Shanghai-Ping regular train to Jinan. He arrived in Jinan at 8:10 PM this evening (the 21st). After getting off the train, he went to the Jinpu Hotel to rest. Kong was accompanied by three people, including Zhu Yong, Secretary of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission and Deputy Chief Engineer of the Closure Office. According to Kong, his trip to Beijing and Shanghai involved reporting on the negotiations and his mission to Jinan as follows:

Kong's Statement

After the breach was closed, I supervised the construction at the site to consolidate the closure project. Then I went to Beijing and reported the closure process and the closure situation to the National Economic Commission and Minister Kong. I received praise and consolation. Later, because Minister Kong went to Shanghai, I also rushed to Shanghai to discuss with him the post-disaster work of the closure and future flood prevention matters. Minister Kong hopes that no further breaches will occur this year under any circumstances and even hopes that flood disasters can be avoided year after year forever. This is indeed Minister Kong's earnest hope for the people, and I think that everyone across the country shares this sentiment. Those of us who are engaged in river projects are especially concerned. The volume of the Yellow River floods is increasing year by year. Last year's flow rate reached a record high of 18,000 cubic meters per second, while the lower reaches of the river channel are gradually narrowing, and the riverbed is silting up higher and higher, reducing the drainage capacity. According to reports, there is a particularly large accumulation of ice and snow in the upper reaches of Gansu and Ningxia this year. When the ice melts in the summer, it can be predicted that the flood situation will be even greater this year. This situation is very worrying. If we do not plan and prepare in advance, it will be difficult to ensure safety. Currently, the opinion of all parties is that to control the Yellow River, it is necessary to organize a unified management agency, unify authority, and take responsibility for overall planning and management to be effective. Minister Kong also strongly advocates this, but because it involves several provinces and the matter is very important, it is necessary to inquire about the opinions of all parties in detail and plan carefully before there can be specific measures. Now it is planned to discuss measures with all parties. In addition to this, repairing the river channel in the lower reaches is also the most important part of this year's flood prevention work. Because river control cannot rely solely on defense, the fundamental solution must be to dredge the river channel to allow the water to flow smoothly. Since the lower reaches have been silted up too high and the water flow is obstructed, it is necessary to find ways to dredge them to make them smooth. However, this project is very large. I heard that the Shandong Construction Department has already surveyed and planned, but because the project is large and expensive, it has not been possible to start construction. My mission to Jinan is to discuss this matter with Chairman Han. Although the cost is very high, it must be done. In the future, in order to save construction costs, we may use military labor. However, everything must be decided after detailed consultation with Chairman Han, Director Zhang, and others. The post-disaster work of the Dongzhuang closure project is currently underway. The new dike, diversion dam, and closure dam have all been raised and thickened. As per the original plan, the reconstruction of the dike is also underway. Most of the Huangzhuang-Linpuji section of the embankment has been completed. The second and third breaches have been completely closed. Work has also begun on the fourth and fifth breaches. There is currently only a small amount of accumulated water in the sixth breach, and the flow has long been cut off. The Zhudong section of the embankment is also under construction. There are also many post-disaster projects and future handover matters to be discussed with Chairman Han. This is also part of my mission to Jinan. Regarding the Zhukou dangerous section, the general public pays close attention to it. I will allocate 30 million cubic meters of stone materials to be built by local people, and I will also provide considerable subsidies. When I was at the construction site, I had already discussed it with the locals, and they are very happy to do so. As for which sections of the Yellow River project are dangerous and which are safe, no one dares to say for sure. Because the Yellow River's water conditions change rapidly, often a dangerous section in the morning becomes stable in the evening, and a stable section today becomes a dangerous section tomorrow. Therefore, it is difficult to answer when asked about the situation in a particular area. In short, although Zhukou is dangerous, it has the protection of 30 million stones and is unlikely to be unexpected. Yangzhuang, Lengzhai, Xiaoxindi, and other places are more worrying and should be paid attention to. I heard Mr. Pei, the vice engineer of the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee, say that in the disaster-stricken areas of Jiangsu and Shandong, most of the land has been dried up and replanting is underway. Because Mr. Pei recently visited the disaster areas of Jiangsu and Shandong in person, what he said about the counties in northern Jiangsu and Juye in Shandong is very accurate. I will not stay in Jinan for long. After meeting with Chairman Han, I will return to the Dongzhuang construction site to supervise the post-disaster work.

Dredging the Yellow River

Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, believes that the Yellow River's riverbed is rising day by day, and future prevention and control will become increasingly difficult. He previously submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to use the method of conscripting labor to dredge the Yellow River estuary, so as to facilitate the outflow of water. It has been approved by the National Economic Commission. It is said that Han has now submitted a request to President Chiang, in addition to stating the recent situation of the Yellow River and requesting active dredging, and also requesting the construction of a railway along the banks, in order to facilitate the transportation of materials and benefit river defense.

Surveying the Lower Reaches

The Shandong River Affairs Bureau starts handling spring engineering projects every year in the spring. This year's spring engineering projects, because last year's disaster relief expenses were huge, the various construction costs for dike repair this year have had to be slightly reduced. In the upper reaches, that is, the construction of the dike from Shilibu to Huanghuasi, which is entirely earthwork, is being supervised by Li Shilin, Director of the Engineering Section of the Bureau, who has gone to supervise the work and started construction. It is reported that four or five tenths of the work has been completed. In another month or so, the entire project will be completed. In the lower reaches, from Wuwangzhuang downward, the dike is also being raised and thickened. The River Affairs Bureau has sent personnel to survey and measure it. As soon as the survey is completed, construction will begin. The Yellow River water level has been continuously dropping for several days. At Luokou on the 20th, the water level dropped six centimeters to 28.34 meters. The labor conditions in the various reaches are stable, and the dangerous sections in the lower reaches have also turned from danger to safety. (21st)

Anhui Rice: Large-Scale Transport and Sale to Guangdong and Hubei 102

Foreign Rice Tax Increase Leads to Sharp Decline in Imports 103

Wuhu Correspondence: Wuhu has always been the pivotal hub for exporting Anhui rice, and the rise and fall of the province's rice market are centered around Wuhu. In recent years, due to the dumping of foreign rice and the barrenness of rice-producing areas, there was almost no rice market to speak of. Rice merchants from the Guangdong and Chaozhou regions specializing in purchasing and transporting rice were mostly desolate. It wasn't until last winter that activity slightly picked up, and exports gradually increased, with various industries also gradually showing signs of vitality. Recently, the rice market has seen another resurgence. Chaozhou merchants such as Tongxin, Changfa, Yifeng, Shunfeng, and Tongfa have collected and transported large quantities, which are successively transported from Wuhu by scheduled ironclad ships to Chaozhou, Shantou, and other places. Following them are merchants such as Fuhe and Fushengxiang, who purchase on behalf of Hubei merchants and transport the rice upstream by river steamers. Statistics show that weekly exports are about 20,000 shi. This kind of foreign trade in Anhui rice has achieved a tremendous turnaround, mainly due to the increased import tax on foreign rice. In recent years, the import volume of foreign rice to the southwestern provinces has been staggering, and even the Yangtze River basin, known for its abundant rice production, has been affected. Since the tax increase, the price of foreign rice has exceeded that of Anhui rice by more than one yuan per shi, causing it to be rejected by buyers. As a result, the source of foreign rice is also decreasing daily. If Anhui rice can maintain a stable market price, the future may be somewhat promising. However, in recent days, the concentrated amount of Wuhu rice has not been very enthusiastic, and the market price has been gradually rising. Top-quality rice reaches nine yuan forty-five cents per shi, while medium and lower qualities are also priced at nine yuan twenty-three cents to eight yuan seventy-eight cents. The reason for this is that the spring famine in various counties in southern Anhui this year is severe. Counties under the jurisdiction of Huizhou are looking forward to assistance from other counties. Hefei, Hanshan, Nanling, and other counties are also taking measures to prevent food shortages, leading to successive bans on rice exports. Therefore, the market price is likely to continue to rise. Whether the foreign trade of Anhui rice can be revived in the future depends on whether the regulation can be appropriate. (22nd)

Nanhai Foshan City: Cracking a Case of Photocopying Counterfeit Money; Details of the Arrest of Kogerlai in Foshan City; Informant's Account of the Defendant's Counterfeiting Activities 104

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong province has recently discovered a series of cases of counterfeiting foreign currency. The first and second cases have been detailed in this newspaper. Unexpectedly, on the 13th of this month, the Xinya Hotel in Foshan City, under the jurisdiction of Nanhai County, cracked a case of three foreigners using surgical techniques to photocopy counterfeit foreign currency for use. The two foreign criminals, Kogerlai and his son John, along with another Russian, Alex, resided in room 206 of the hotel. They used chemicals to photocopy foreign banknotes, making copies indistinguishable from the real ones. Later, a traveler in the neighboring room, Mr. Wu, noticed this. Kogerlai asked Wu to find investors to photocopy a large amount of foreign currency for profit. Wu considered it illegal and went to the First Branch of the Foshan Public Security Bureau to report it. The branch chief, Mao Zici, went to investigate and confirmed the facts. He then arrested the three foreigners and sent them to the Nanhai County Office, which transferred them to the Finance Department for interrogation. At noon on the 16th, Wu Rang, the director of the trial division of the Finance Department, interrogated the three foreigners. The head of the secretariat of the Finance Department and others were also present to question them. First, Kogerlai's handcuffs were removed, and he was ordered to photocopy a banknote on the spot using chemicals. However, the photocopying result showed that the white paper did not take on any color. Upon examining the chemicals, it appeared to be a type of Western medicine (Bengxian in transliteration). Kogerlai claimed that he had not counterfeited any foreign currency in the Foshan hotel. The counterfeit money presented as evidence was also genuine, but at the time, he had only altered the last digit of the banknote number as a prank and did not intend to photocopy counterfeit money. After the trial director's interrogation, he believed that the case of photocopying banknotes required detailed interrogation and should not be treated lightly. Therefore, on the 18th, he transferred the case, along with the suspects and evidence, to the Guangzhou Local Court Procuratorate for investigation. In the afternoon of the same day at 4 pm, Prosecutor Lu of the Procuratorate opened the court and interrogated the suspect in the case. He first questioned the informant, Wu Hanglin. According to Wu Zhilin's account, at noon on the 10th of this month, Kogerlai, John, and Alex also arrived at the Xinya Hotel in Foshan and stayed in room 206. The next day, because they were not familiar with the language, the waiters were troubled by them. Wu, witnessing the situation, occasionally helped with translation. As a result, Kogerlai became acquainted with Wu. On the 13th, Kogerlai asked him if he was a Christian. Wu replied that he had been baptized for ten years. Kogerlai considered him a fellow believer and said that he had something to discuss, but it was a secret and required an oath of secrecy before he could tell him. Wu then performed a religious oath ceremony as requested. After the oath, Kogerlai immediately told Wu that they had a wonderful method to photocopy various banknotes. They had used it extensively in Beijing, Tianjin, Hong Kong, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Wuzhou, and other places. He asked Wu to raise capital on his behalf. Since Wu became acquainted with them, they had used the copied counterfeit money many times. Wu believed that this kind of behavior was not tolerated by the law. On the 13th, he rushed to report to Mao Zici, the chief of the First Branch of the Foshan Public Security Bureau, and the Yue Detective Team of Nanhai County. Mao then pretended to be a millionaire and went to visit Kogerlai at the hotel with Wu. Afterwards, Mao reported to the Nanhai County Administrative Office, which dispatched a detective team of fourteen people to lie in ambush. Then Wu and Mao entered to visit. Kogerlai was already seated. Wu introduced Mao's intentions. Mao pretended to be investing in a company. Kogerlai believed it to be true and ordered Mao to swear to heaven. After Mao swore, Kogerlai immediately took out a ten-yuan banknote from the Hong Kong and Shanghai Bank, along with two blank sheets of paper, and photocopied them with chemicals. Mao waited until he finished the process and then gave a signal, ordering the detectives to arrest Kogerlai and others along with the evidence. This was the situation at the time of the case's cracking. He requested to be released on bail. The judge then interrogated the three foreigners in English. According to Kogerlai's statement, he was 34 years old, from Persia, and had been in China for fifteen years. He had first gone to Shanghai, Nanjing, and Peiping (Beijing) and had served in a police academy in Guangxi. He had only recently arrived in Guangdong. As for the counterfeit money, it was not made by him. It was all found on Wu's person. As for his trip to Foshan, he went with Wu. He claimed that he did not engage in any counterfeiting activities. John stated that he was 15 years old and was Kogerlai's son. Alex stated that he was 20 years old, Russian, and a friend of Kogerlai. They both denied any involvement in counterfeiting. After the interrogation, Prosecutor Lu detained Kogerlai and others in the detention center to await further investigation. Wu Zhilin was temporarily granted bail with a guarantor from a shop and was subject to call at any time. (April 19th)

Songjiang: Civil Servants Dredge City River 105

Various agencies in the county are implementing a labor service program for civil servants, designated by the county government to dredge a section of the city river from Fengle Bridge to Hezhuang Bridge, with a length of approximately 300 meters, a dredging depth of 1.00 and 0.80, and a bottom width of four meters. On the morning of the 23rd at 7:30 am, more than 600 civil servants from various agencies gathered in the public sports field. At 8:00 am, an opening ceremony was held, presided over by Shen Zongliang, secretary acting as county magistrate, and Commissioner Wang gave a speech. Subsequently, Wang Zhezhou of the Party Committee and Zhang Yongling of the Independent Detachment of the 12th Security Brigade delivered speeches. Thirty groups from the Party, government, military, and schools participated, lining up and departing in order, parading through the streets for a week to the construction site, each working according to the divided sections. The river project was originally scheduled to be completed in three days, but some were quite diligent in their work. Therefore, the First District Office and the County Party Headquarters completed the work at 4:00 pm that afternoon.

Farmers in Su Township, Guoxiang, and Xietang Township previously rioted over rent. On the morning of the 23rd, Magistrate Deng again took a motorboat to Zhouzhuang Township, summoning the township and village chiefs for a lecture, advising farmers to clear their rent arrears within this month. He returned to the city that evening and will go to Wei Township again today (24th) to continue advising farmers to pay their rent.

Demanding Wages, Blood Splatters in Teahouse 110

Meng Yuanzhai of Malu Township and Yang Longyun, a resident of the village, recently contracted the earthwork for the central section of the Su-Xi Highway from Wangting to Mucheng. At that time, they subcontracted it to foremen such as Chen San and Xiang Fa. Since the start of construction, they have built more than 1,500 cubic meters of highway. At around 6 pm the night before, the foremen, Chen San and others, led dozens of workers to Yang's house to demand wages. Because the Construction Department had not yet inspected and accepted the road surface and the amount was incorrect, Yang could not pay them immediately. They refused to leave until night. After mutual scuffling, they were brought to the bureau, and both sides were persuaded to mediate. On the morning of the 22nd at around 10 am, the workers again dragged Yang to the Longyuan Teahouse on Malu Road, threatening him in every way and forcing him to hand over the wages. Dozens of workers surrounded Yang, each holding sharp blades, and attacking him. At that time, Yang's head was stabbed with a knife, about an inch deep and four inches wide, with blood flowing freely. His hands, shoulders, and other parts were also severely injured by the knives. He immediately fell to the ground, his life hanging by a thread. The patrol officer from that area arrived after hearing the news and arrested the murderers, Chen San, Xiang Tongfa, Ding Jinyuan, Jin Wansheng, and others. They were transferred to the General Bureau and then to the court for interrogation and detention. The injured Yang Longyun was sent to the Brothers Hospital for treatment.

Local News

Fourteen Foreign Tea Firms Suspend Exchange Yesterday; Telegraphs Sent for Assistance; City Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs President Chiang to Intervene; Orders Anhui Provincial Government to Maintain Original Agreement on Commercial Sales 111

After the Foreign Tea Firms Association issued a declaration on the Anhui Province's control over the transport and sale of Qihong tea, they uniformly suspended exchange yesterday morning and telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce, etc., to report. The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed Chairman Chiang, the National Economic Commission, and the Anhui Provincial Government, requesting that the original agreement on commercial sales be maintained to show good faith. The Foreign Tea Firms Association also petitioned Zhu Ziwen, a standing committee member of the Economic Commission, for assistance. Details are recorded separately below:

Implementation of Suspension of Exchange: The fourteen foreign tea firms, including Zhongxinchang, Hongyuanyong, Yongxinglong, Zhenhe, Yitai, Yuanfengrun, Gongshengyong, Shenyuan, Rendeyong, Shengchangsheng, Yilong, Xietai, Tongqin, and Xielong, uniformly followed the resolution of the industry association yesterday morning and suspended the exchange of promissory notes issued by various tea firms to tea merchants in Anhui, totaling more than one million yuan, with varying terms. The association also telegraphed the Anhui Tea Industry Association and the Chamber of Commerce, saying: "To the Tea Industry Association and the Chamber of Commerce, regarding the Anhui Province's control over the transport and sale of black tea, this association and the City Chamber of Commerce have repeatedly requested, but the agreement has been repeatedly overturned or even ignored, placing the tea firms in a desperate situation. We have been forced to publish a declaration that all export tea firms will immediately suspend the exchange of notes. Sincerely, Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association."

Telegram from Tea Manufacturing Industry:

"To Chairman Liu Jun of the Anhui Provincial Government, foreign tea firms have announced their closure due to the control of black tea. More than forty firms in the city of Shanghai rely on the loans from foreign tea firms to support their business. Now that the foreign tea firms have announced their closure, our industry has suddenly lost its financial support, and business will inevitably be difficult. More than forty firms are affected by this, and the livelihood of thousands of workers is cut off, making their lives precarious. Furthermore, tea producers in the producing areas have no one to buy their tea, causing millions of farmers to suffer even more. At this time when tea is being produced, please do not endanger the national export tea industry due to the control of a part, causing it to suffer a setback. We dare to implore you to consider maintaining the foreign tea firms, which is the same as maintaining our industry, and can also help the tea-producing farmers. We make this urgent request, hoping for your consideration. Sincerely, Shanghai Tea Manufacturing Industry Association (stamped)."

Telegram from Economic Commission: The National Economic Commission replied to the City Chamber of Commerce, saying, "To the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, your telegram is acknowledged. We have previously approved your respectful telegram, stating that the joint establishment of a black tea transport and sales committee by Anhui and Jiangxi provinces affects the business of tea firms. We have transferred it to the Anhui Provincial Government for investigation and handling. We have received a reply stating that the black tea produced in Anhui and Jiangxi provinces is of excellent quality and is a precious product among black teas. It originally had a special position in export trade, but because tea merchants and tea farmers have never had a proper organization for liaison, they are subject to manipulation and exploitation, and sales are not free. This has led to a daily decrease in production and a decline in sales. Since it is related to international trade and affects the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people, the provincial government's duty is not to stand idly by. With the consent of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, a black tea transport and sales committee was established to be responsible for improving transport and sales, and the establishment meeting was held in Anqing on April 1st of this year to discuss the implementation plan. The resolutions discussed are all based on the entire black tea industry, intending to unify transport and sales to avoid manipulation and exploitation, and do not hinder the loans of tea firms. As for the concerns about the unemployment and creditor's rights of tea firms, the following three proposals have been resolved to provide relief: (1) To recruit talents from tea firms as much as possible to assist in the committee's affairs; (2) If a creditor submits an amount that the debtor acknowledges should be repaid, the committee's sales office will summon both parties after the tea is sold to handle it according to custom. If there are disputes, the two parties will resolve them according to law; (3) For those tea merchants who have already accepted loans from tea firms this year, after the products of the tea merchant are sold out in the future, the proceeds from the tea price, after deducting commissions and advances, will be handed over to the original lender to settle accounts with the tea merchant. If the original lender voluntarily withdraws the loan, before the product is shipped, if the qualifications of the tea merchant and the amount of the loan meet the committee's approval and are verified to be true, the loan and interest will be transferred. As far as the tea firms in Shanghai that operate the export of black tea are concerned, there are only six, and they all also operate green tea, the quantity of which exceeds black tea several times. The various problems regarding black tea are not very serious. Now that various relief measures have been resolved, the tea firms do not need to worry too much." The telegram was previously approved. The Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association has sent representatives to Anhui to propose four compromise opinions. The Provincial Government should also verify and handle the matter according to the opinions proposed by the representatives. Sincerely, Ma (stamped), National Economic Commission. The contents of the letter from the National Economic Commission to the Foreign Tea Firms Association are roughly the same, omitted.

Reply to Economic Commission: "To the National Economic Commission in Nanjing, Ma's telegram is respectfully acknowledged. The reply from the Anhui Provincial Government to your commission contains many evasions and unutterable truths. The Anhui Province's control of Qihong tea this time uses the banner of improving transport and sales, but the so-called control and improvement are not synonymous with provincial operations. Now Anhui Province is independently lending money and independently selling, replacing the position of tea firms. This is using a control policy for tea merchants and an extermination policy for tea firms, while using gentle words of comfort in advance. Once the arrangement is in place, it indicates that it is difficult to reverse the decision. What is this called? The so-called recruiting of talents from tea firms to assist in the committee's affairs is nothing more than ordering them to change from shop owners to shop employees. The so-called submitting of amounts and acknowledging repayment is also no different from ordering them to close down and protect their creditor's rights. These are not the state's intentions to protect the legitimate business of the people. This matter is of great importance to the people's economy. Now that the tea firms have implemented a suspension of exchange and closure, the thirty million export tea industry will immediately stop, and the situation is urgent and the impact is extremely large. It is difficult for your commission to ignore this matter. We still request that you intervene and urgently telegraph Anhui Province to achieve a reversal. Sincerely, Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce (stamped)."

Telegram to President Chiang: "Urgent, Kunming, addressed to President Chiang of the Executive Yuan: The establishment of a black tea transport and sales committee by Anhui Province, which brings the tea firm industry that operates foreign export tea after the opening of ports into provincial management, causing tea merchants to lose their jobs, has been repeatedly telegraphed to your Yuan by the affiliated association. Approval was granted for the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to consult with Anhui Province to handle the matter properly. The tea merchants also personally went to Anhui Province to earnestly negotiate and agree on provincial management for transport and commercial management for sales, striving to leave a chance for the merchants to survive. Unexpectedly, Anhui Province still has changes to the case presented in person. Under the transport and sales committee, a sales group is established, allowing it to recruit talents from tea firms to handle the matter, which is equivalent to officials selling on their own and merchants serving as shop employees, fundamentally exterminating the tea firms. Efforts to appeal have been exhausted, and the tea firms have been forced to stop exchanging and close down all notes issued from today. We believe that Qihong tea is a major export trade, and tea firms have a history of nearly a century. As matters stand, it not only affects foreign sales and affects Shanghai's financial industry, but also officials seize commercial opportunities, making merchants' legitimate businesses lose all protection. This is of great concern to national credibility and public sentiment. Considering that you are admired by the whole country and all matters of state rely on your fair judgment, since there is nothing to appeal to in Anhui Province, we must respectfully petition your seat, urgently request your intervention, and order the Anhui Provincial Government to maintain the original agreement on commercial sales to show good faith and maintain the lifeblood of export tea merchants. Sincerely, Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce (stamped)."

Reply from Anhui Province: "To the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, your telegram has been read and acknowledged. The Anhui and Jiangxi provinces' improvement of black tea transport and sales this time takes into account both tea farmers and tea merchants. If the tea firms can eliminate the various exploitations of tea merchants in the past, reduce the monthly interest rate on loans to eight percent, and listen to the transport and sales committee's unification of transport with the most convenient methods, and the sales are subject to the supervision and command of the transport and sales office, the committee can recruit talents from tea firms as much as possible to undertake sales affairs. All two percent of the commission can be waived from deduction by the committee. According to the situation presented by the tea firm representatives who came to Anhui in person, we have clearly informed them. There are some discrepancies between the points raised in the presentation by the Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association and the informed method, and instructions have also been issued. If the Foreign Tea Firms Association can sincerely accept this, it will be beneficial to both public and private interests. The general transport and sales office of the transport and sales committee will send personnel to Shanghai to set up a sales group immediately, which can be contacted nearby for handling. I hope you will persuade them not to cause disturbances. Sincerely, Liu Zhenhua, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government (stamped)." "To the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, your telegram has been read and acknowledged. Telegram is to announce the resolution of the transport and sales committee. is to instruct the tea firm representatives on the method. According to the presentation from the Shanghai Foreign Tea Firms Association, instructions have been issued to still follow the method shown in the telegram and sincerely negotiate with the Shanghai transport and sales office for handling. We have also telegraphed your Chamber of Commerce in detail on the same day. The matter concerns the revitalization of the tea industry, and the government's promulgation of laws and regulations is difficult to change. I hope you will explain this and handle it according to the telegram. Do not put yourselves in a desperate situation. Sincerely, Chairman Liu Zhenhua (stamped)."

Telegram to Anhui Province Again: "To the Anhui Provincial Government in Huaining, the two telegrams have been respectfully acknowledged and forwarded to the Foreign Tea Firms Association, which stated that the key points presented in person in Anhui Province have been completely overturned. What is this called? Now that all the tea firms have stopped exchanging and closed down, the thirty million export tea industry has immediately stopped. As matters stand, this association is also at the end of its persuasion. We humbly report this. Sincerely, Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce (stamped)."

Petition to Song for Assistance: "The Foreign Tea Firms Association yesterday presented to Song Ziwen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Commission, saying, 'The Anhui Province's control of black tea transport and sales aims to provincial management and monopoly, competing with the people for profits. Its previous expressions to our industry have been extremely strange and changeable. At first, it agreed that it would not hinder the loans of tea firms, and then it agreed to accommodate the compromise plan proposed by the petition representatives. However, these were all promises that were quickly overturned. It also sent personnel to Qimen and other producing areas to actively lend money, which has caused the previous debts of tea firms and the loans issued this year to lose protection. It has also deprived the loan business and tea sales business that have been followed for decades since the opening of ports without leaving anything behind. It is feared that its intentions will intensify and expand to control even green tea. The industry is deeply afraid of this. An emergency meeting was convened and resolved to suspend exchange and close down from the 21st. The City Chamber of Commerce comforted us and postponed the implementation for two days. At the same time, we urgently telegraphed Anhui Province, requesting that it accommodate us according to the previously agreed-upon method. However, up until yesterday afternoon, we did not receive a request. If we do not earnestly implement the previous resolution, it will not be enough to seek self-preservation. All the details can be seen in the declaration and do not need to be elaborated. The people's freedom to operate is clearly permitted by law, and the special privileges of industrial and commercial rights belong to the central government. The laws of the period of political tutelage also have clear regulations, which cannot be decided by any local government without authorization. Moreover, export trade affects the people's livelihood and the national economy. Even if merchants' hard-earned capital can be ignored, the local economy and the nation's vitality are at stake. How can we allow those with no experience to try as they please? The industry, in order to preserve business capital and take into account the national industry, besides enduring the pain of sacrifice and waiting quietly for a solution, should report the matter in detail and respectfully ask you to quickly provide assistance so that the people's livelihood will not perish together with the tea firm business in one fell swoop. We will be forever grateful.''"

Impact on Charitable Donations: "The Shanghai Huining Guild Hall telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government yesterday regarding the Anhui Province's control of Qihong tea transport and sales, saying, 'To Chairman Liu of the Anhui Provincial Government, since the guild hall was established in Shanghai, the annual expenses required for charitable acts such as providing coffins and clothes, medical assistance, and burying coffins have all relied on the box donations solicited by the Foreign Tea Firms. This means that the government is directly placing the Foreign Tea Firms in a desperate situation, and indirectly causing the guild hall's charitable work to be suspended. The guild hall and the Foreign Tea Firms are closely related and cannot remain silent. We are therefore telegraphing you to request that you verify and handle the matter quickly to maintain the tea firms' business. We are anxiously awaiting your orders. Sincerely, Shanghai Huining Guild Hall (stamped).'"

The Ning Shao Steamer Encountered a Great Peril on the Huangzhou River 113

A Sudden Attack of Wind, Rain, and Hail in the Deep Dark Night Caused Both Anchors to Break – A Perilous Voyage Luckily Reached Jiujiang

The Old Ning Shao Steamer of the Ning Shao Steamer Company in this port, built in 1906, with a deadweight of 3,074 tons, a registered tonnage of 1,920 tons, a length of 283 feet, a breadth of 44 feet 7 inches, a depth of 16 feet 6 inches, a draft of 10 feet, and a speed of 12 nautical miles per hour, has always sailed

on long shifts. It was decided that this steamer would load a large quantity of goods and passengers in Hankou and depart downstream to Shanghai on the afternoon of the 21st. When the ship set sail, the weather was very good with no wind or waves. Unexpectedly, at 12 o'clock that night, when it reached the Huangzhou River upstream of Jiujiang, the weather suddenly changed. First, a torrential rain poured down like a waterfall, and then a strong wind rose, shaking trees and mountains. Huge waves stirred up in the middle of the river, and finally,

hail fell suddenly, as large as pebbles. The deep night was as dark as pitch, and the river surface was indistinguishable within a short distance. At this time, the Ning Shao Steamer was under attack by heavy rain, hurricane, hail, and fierce waves, and a very dangerous situation arose on the river. The ship shook violently, and the passengers were terrified. It is said that the captain, seeing this situation, found it difficult to continue sailing. For the sake of the safety of the lives and property of the entire ship, he had to temporarily stop and quickly

drop both anchors, hoping to wait for the storm to pass before sailing again. However, the wind, rain, and hail continued to fall madly, and the waves on the river were stirred up by the strong wind, coming like mountains toppling over and seas overturning. The Ning Shao Steamer dropped both anchors, thinking that it would be safe, but who knew that the force of the wind and waves was impacting the hull of the ship, and the ship still could not withstand it, causing the thick iron chains of both anchors to crackle and clang under the impact of the huge waves and strong wind. Then, with a loud bang,

both anchors broke and sank to the bottom of the river. The mooring chains also broke off more than 75 fathoms, and the swaying of the ship became even more dangerous. It is said that the captain decisively started the engine at this time, braving all difficulties and sailing downstream at great risk. By good fortune, it safely reached Jiujiang on the morning of the 22nd, preserving the lives and property of the entire ship. When it arrived at Xunyang, all the passengers on board looked at each other with joy. The captain temporarily borrowed two anchors from another ship for

emergency navigation. Yesterday, the captain telegraphed from Xunyang to Shanghai, stating, in brief, that the Old Ning Shao Steamer, around 12 o'clock on the evening of the 21st, encountered heavy rain, hurricane, and hail in the Huangzhou River, and the weather was unusually dark, making it impossible to see anything on the river surface. For safety, he dropped both anchors, but unexpectedly both anchors broke, leaving no other option but to risk sailing downstream. By good fortune, it arrived at Xunyang at 8 o'clock on the morning of the 22nd and has now borrowed two anchors from a Man steamer for emergency use. Please quickly prepare anchor chains of 75 fathoms and transport them for use, and so on. After receiving the telegram, the Ning Shao Company has already prepared the heavy chains and transported them.

The Shokoku Collided with the Wan Tai at the 15th Pier in Dalian 114

All Crew Members Were Fortunately Rescued, Resulting in a Loss of 70,000 to 80,000 Yuan. The Wan Tai, owned by the Zhaoxing Shipping Company in this port, which specializes in traveling to the Dalian Bay area of North China, was unloading cargo at the 15th pier in Dalian yesterday morning when the Shokoku Maru (a European liner) of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company was turning around at the same location and violently struck the Wan Tai's left stern, creating a large hole. The Wan Tai, with a displacement of just over 700 tons, suffered extensive damage from the impact of the vessel, which displaced over 10,000 tons. The vessel sank in just 15 minutes, but fortunately, all of the crew members were rescued. The damage is estimated to be 70,000 to 80,000 Yuan, and the responsibility lies entirely with the Japanese vessel. The company had insured the vessel for 60,000 Yuan through the China Ship Insurance United Association and notified the association yesterday.

The Huai River Conservancy Board Borrowed 3.3 Million from Three Banks 115

Each of the Central, China, and Communications Banks Lends 1.1 Million Yuan – Agreement Reached, Funds to be Released as Needed for the Project

The Huai River Conservancy Board previously borrowed 4 million yuan from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board for the construction of the Sanhe movable dam and the Huai River diversion project into the sea, to purchase materials and cover construction costs. At the same time, it also borrowed funds from the banking sector for use. According to information obtained by a Xin Xin News Agency reporter, the Huai River Conservancy project is progressing rapidly, and most of the borrowed funds have been allocated in installments. However, the project is now in urgent need of progress and cannot be delayed. After consultations with the Central, China, and Communications Banks, the three banks have agreed to lend 1.1 million yuan each, for a total of 3.3 million yuan. Agreements have been reached and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for record. The method of disbursing the funds stipulates that they will be released as needed for the project.

The Fourth Day of the Anti-Smoking Propaganda Week: Yesterday, Performers Throughout the City Reject Drugs; Today, All Theaters Will Show Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Films; Tomorrow, Various Groups Will Organize Propaganda Teams to Set Off for Propaganda 118

The Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week jointly organized by the City Party Headquarters and various circles in this city held its fourth day yesterday (23rd), which was the propaganda day for performers. More than 3,000 performers throughout the city separately promoted the meaning of anti-smoking and anti-drug. Students from Shanghai Girls' Middle School paraded in formation yesterday afternoon. Today is the film propaganda day, and all cinemas in the city will show anti-smoking and anti-drug films. Tomorrow is the propaganda day for various groups, and various groups will organize propaganda teams on this day, and the Juvenile Propaganda Corps will dress up for propaganda. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Yesterday, the Performers' Propaganda Day

More Than 3,000 Performers Propagandized

Yesterday (23rd) was the fourth day of Propaganda Week, which, according to the prescribed procedure, was the performers' propaganda day. The preparatory committee had printed propaganda outlines in advance and consulted with the Shanghai Performers' Association. All members of the association were fully mobilized for propaganda, totaling more than 3,000 people. They served as performers in various entertainment venues such as Yong'an, Sincere, New World, Shanghai New World, Great Thousand World, Great World, and Small World, as well as in Suzhou opera, monologue, Shanghai storytelling, Pinghua ballad singing, drama and other venues, and film broadcasting, all interspersing the meaning of anti-smoking and anti-drug.

Shanghai Girls' Middle School Paraded Enthusiastically

The Shanghai Girls' Middle School in Xieqiao took anti-smoking and anti-drug as the late Premier's legacy, the government is determined to eliminate it, and the public should cooperate and promote it. Not only should students understand this meaning, but the general public should also pay attention. Therefore, they specially made many cloth and paper slogans and pictures, and at 2:00 p.m. yesterday, they ordered all students to set off in a parade. Led by the Boy Scout band, the road was blocked wherever they went, and the atmosphere was very enthusiastic. The audience paid a lot of attention.

Minli Girls' Middle School Continued Lectures

The Minli Girls' Middle School on Wenmiao Road in Nanshi, because the academic propaganda day for the Anti-Smoking and Anti-Drug Propaganda Week on the previous day coincided with rain, making it inconvenient to set off, sent more than 20 students to organize a propaganda team to carry out supplementary propaganda yesterday morning and afternoon. A reporter from the National News Agency went to the Nine Mu Di yesterday and happened to hear the propaganda team giving a lecture, which was very moving to the listeners. According to news from the City Education Association, there were other schools that carried out supplementary propaganda yesterday.

Today is Film Propaganda Day

All Theaters in the City Will Show Additional Films

Today is the fifth day of Propaganda Week, which belongs to the film propaganda day. The preparatory committee specially made a large number of anti-smoking and anti-drug films in advance and sent them to Jin Cheng, Star, Shanxi, New Central, West Sea, East Sea, Central, Guanghua, World, Jinrong, Carde, Huade, Republic, Shanghai, Penglai, Wanguo and other cinemas in this port for additional screenings, so that the audience would know the harm of smoking and drugs. It is heard that these films have been screened in various theaters since the 20th to assist the government in eliminating the atmosphere of drugs.

Commanders and Disciplinarians Are Mostly Appointed

As the date for the lantern parade is approaching, the preparatory committee has written to various agencies and organizations, in order to unify command in all circles, asking them to appoint a general commander, deputy commander, general disciplinarian, and deputy disciplinarian. It is now heard that those who have been appointed include Lin Meiyan as the general commander of the City Party Headquarters, Chen Weiyi as the deputy commander, Zhang Xiaotong as the general disciplinarian, Zhang Yingzeng as the deputy disciplinarian, Zheng Zeguang as the general commander of the Public Security Bureau, Xie Xiumian as the deputy commander, Wang Yupei as the general disciplinarian, Ding Shunbao as the deputy disciplinarian, Yu Zhenhui as the general commander of the City Farmers' Association, Zhang Huijun as the general disciplinarian, Yuan Hongjun as the general commander of the City Chamber of Commerce, Xin Jianxin as the deputy commander, Li Fanglan as the general disciplinarian, Wang Rongkun as the deputy disciplinarian, Huang Zaoxiong as the general commander of the City Education Association, Zhang Lichun as the deputy commander, Wang Longzhang as the general disciplinarian, and Huang Kegui as the deputy disciplinarian.

Tomorrow is the Propaganda Day for Various Groups

Various Groups Will Organize Propaganda Teams

Tomorrow (25th) is the sixth day of Propaganda Week, which is the propaganda day for various groups according to regulations. The preparatory committee convened a discussion meeting with representatives of various groups a few days ago, and the City Farmers' Association, the General Labor Union, the City Chamber of Commerce, the Education Association, the Boy Scout Council, and the Anti-Drug Association will conduct propaganda separately, and each has ordered its subordinates to organize propaganda teams and go to various places for propaganda and lectures, following the organizational methods of party member and student propaganda teams.

Children's Groups' Costume Lecture Meeting

Tomorrow is the propaganda day for various groups, and they are extremely enthusiastic about various propaganda activities. This time, the City Party Headquarters is holding an anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda week. In order to make citizens understand the harm of smoking and drugs, the group has specially decided to hold a costume lecture from 8:00 p.m. to 12:00 p.m. tomorrow. Nearby residents are welcome to attend.

Registering to Quit Smoking Costs Nothing

When a reporter from the National News Agency passed by the Nine Mu Di the day before yesterday, he saw several propaganda teams from the Party Headquarters giving lectures on anti-smoking. There were many listeners. Someone said that registering with the Public Security Bureau requires a fee, and asking for help in quitting smoking requires a guarantor. The reporter learned yesterday from a spokesperson of the City Party Headquarters that there is now a type of certificate for the poor that costs nothing. Furthermore, in order to take care of the poor, if someone is determined to quit smoking, they only need to have a friend with a legitimate occupation as a guarantor, and there is no need to pay any additional fees.

Yang Hu Speaks on the Meaning of Rejecting Drugs

Central News Agency reports that Songhu Garrison Commander Yang Hu spoke at the Greater China Radio Station from 3:00 p.m. to 4:00 p.m. the day before yesterday (22nd). His words were as follows: Fellow citizens, brothers, I am usually very busy with official duties and rarely have the opportunity to meet and talk with you. Today, I am taking the opportunity of this city's anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda week to speak with you, fellow citizens, as if we were speaking in the same room, which I find very pleasant. I believe that many of you already know the harms of opium and drugs. Today, due to time constraints, I can only briefly talk about the meaning of anti-smoking and anti-drug. I hope that after everyone hears it, they will persuade each other. This is not only a supplement to the current anti-smoking and anti-drug propaganda, but also has a great relationship with the future of our revitalizing the Chinese nation. Examining the history of the spread of opium and drugs to China, it first came from India. It was not until the Daoguang period of the late Qing Dynasty that British merchants transported it to China in large quantities. At that time, our countrymen did not know the advantages and disadvantages and bought and smoked it with each other, so that in just a few years, the number of people who smoked opium gradually increased. At that time, Mr. Lin Zexu of Guangdong and Guangxi, seeing the harm of opium, not only could it destroy the country, but it was enough to exterminate the race. Therefore, he resolutely implemented a ban on people smoking opium. At the same time, he burned the imported opium regardless of everything. Unexpectedly, the United Kingdom protested and demanded compensation, which led to the Opium War. At that time, because our country lacked military preparedness, the result was a defeat. From then on, the shackles of all unequal treaties were tightened day by day, and the national situation became increasingly depressed. Therefore, from the history of the Opium War, we can see that opium is not only a poisonous substance that gradually weakens our country's physique, but also a dangerous step that causes our country's national status to decline. Fellow compatriots with blood and spirit, don't you feel heartbroken about this? Citizens with this bad habit, shouldn't you quickly make up your minds to quit it? Furthermore, from the perspective of the people who smoke opium and drugs themselves, which one is not physically weak and mentally depressed? They naturally have no energy to do personal business on weekdays, and they are even less able to shoulder their due responsibilities to society, the country, and the nation. Can a country of sick men and a country full of smoking and drugs still compete for existence in the twenty-first century, where the fittest survive? If this harm is not removed, the entire Chinese nation will probably have no foothold on the earth. Now that our country and nation are weakening day by day, and the future is unknown how serious it will be, our leader Chairman Chiang, in order to revitalize our nation and protect the entire country, promulgated 13 articles of the Smuggling Prohibition Implementation Measures and 12 articles of the Drug Prohibition Implementation Measures last year, and established the Smuggling Prohibition Headquarters, with Chairman Chiang serving as the director. These two measures are extremely strict, and the time limit is also very short. If people with smoking and drug addictions do not quickly register in accordance with the regulations and quickly take medicine to quit, they will have no chance of self-renewal in the future. Even if we do not have the idea of saving the country and seeking survival, and we do not have the ambition to defend the country, do we not pay attention to protecting our own bodies and saving our own lives? Citizens from all walks of life, you must know that Chairman Chiang also serves as the director of Smuggling Prohibition, and his words are followed by law. Our revolutionary government will never follow the old ways and compromise. Haven't you seen that in the capital Beijing and Shanghai, many drug dealers of red and white pills have been shot? Citizens from all walks of life, now is the time for us to save ourselves and seek survival. The government will never relax its efforts on this anti-smuggling policy, which is related to the safety of the entire nation. Our citizens who have bad habits should be decisive and hold the determination to die rather than violate the ban, and quickly get out of the sea of suffering. Think carefully, for yourself and for the nation, you should not delay any longer.

The Deadline for Exchanging Legal Tender is Approaching; Banks are Crowded with People Exchanging Money; Silver Deposits in Legal Tender Circulation Areas Must Be Exchanged Before the Deadline; Various Departments in Border Areas Plan to Devise Flexible Measures to Remedy the Situation 119

Shen Shi News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance stipulates that the deadline for exchanging silver deposits for legal tender will expire on the 3rd of next month. Those who still fail to exchange after the deadline will be sentenced to imprisonment. Therefore, banks have been very crowded with people exchanging legal tender in recent days. It is expected that before the 3rd of next month, all silver deposits in areas where legal tender circulates will be exchanged without remainder. It is learned that the Ministry of Finance believes that there are still many areas in border provinces where legal tender has not yet circulated, and people's silver deposits may not be able to be exchanged for legal tender within the deadline. To take care of the interests of the people in the border areas, it is currently studying flexible measures to remedy the situation. As for private silver deposits in areas where legal tender circulates, they must be exchanged for legal tender within the deadline to avoid unexpected losses and being sentenced to imprisonment.

Xue Cixin Returned to Shanghai Yesterday After Inspecting Highway Conditions in Europe and America 120

Xue Cixin, Chief of the Third Section of the Municipal Works Bureau of this city, was dispatched by the National Economic Commission and the Municipal Government to investigate the situation abroad. After spending half a year traveling through European and American countries, he returned to the country and arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 1:00 p.m. aboard the German Mail Steamer "Bausden." Those who went to welcome him included Li Dachao, Section Chief of the Municipal Government, Shen Yi, Director of the Works Bureau, Li Ting'an, Director of the Health Bureau, Tan Wenqing, Xu Guansan, Qiu Xiejun, and Xiao Qingyun, Section Chiefs of the Works Bureau, Wu Liguo, Section Chief of the Health Bureau, Chen Zonghan, Section Chief of the Public Utilities Bureau, Engineer Dong Dayou, and dozens of Xue's relatives and friends. After landing, he went straight to his private residence to rest. According to a written statement issued by Xue to a reporter from the Central News Agency,

Traveling Through Various Countries

This time, Xue Cixin was dispatched by the National Economic Commission and the Shanghai Municipal Government to investigate road administration in Europe and America. Since October 1st of last year, he traveled by the same ship with Mr. Ao Jingji, a consultant of the League of Nations' experts, to the United States and then to Europe, visiting eight countries including England, France, Germany, and the United States, for a period of nearly seven months. After arriving in San Francisco in the United States, he changed to a car and traveled along the southern highway of the United States, passing through ten provinces including California and New Mexico, to the US capital Washington, where he met Mr. McDonald, the director of the highway department there, and thanked him for his kindness in sending engineers to receive him along the way. The highways traveled in the United States totaled more than 8,500 kilometers, lasting 30 days. There are detailed highway maps and various route signs in all the places passed, so even though the people and places are unfamiliar, there is no risk of getting lost. Gas stations and travelers are available along the way, so car travel in the country is very convenient. After staying in Washington for a few days, he went to New York, took the European steamer across the Atlantic Ocean, and arrived in Chabaden, France, and then traveled by car through France and Switzerland to Berlin, the capital of Germany, for a total of more than 3,000 kilometers. He stayed for ten days, and Consultant Ao took the car back to Warsaw, Poland. Cixin stayed in Berlin for inspection for a month and a half. Thanks to the introduction of Director Shen, he met Dr. Todt, the chief engineer of the German national highway. In late January, he left Germany for Poland and stayed in Warsaw for ten days. He is still grateful for the hospitality of the Ministry of Transportation of that country and Consultant Ao. Later, he took the road to Rome, Paris, and then to London, the capital of England. Thanks to the introduction of Zhao, Deputy Director of the Economic Commission, he met Sir Brice, the chief engineer of roads of the British Ministry of Transportation. After staying in England for inspection for a month and a half, he took the German ship "Bausden" back to China.

Investigation Situation

This time, what Cixin investigated in the United States was mostly crude oil roads and asphalt roads. What was investigated in Germany and Poland was stone roads and cement roads. What was inspected in England was the method of building roads with gas asphalt, and more attention was paid to the collection and testing of road building materials. What Cixin saw this time was that road administration in various countries is very developed, but the construction of new roads and the improvement of old roads are still constantly being carried out. Moreover, in the construction of road surfaces, more emphasis is placed on the use of domestic materials and less on the policy of purchasing foreign raw materials, which impressed Cixin too deeply. There are also dozens of kinds of road surface construction methods, but because of the different raw materials and economic conditions, there are not many that can be directly adopted by our country. Because of the need to solve the road surface problem of our country's highways, it still depends on our own efforts and research in the future to find a way out, and the spirit of European and American engineers to use domestic materials to build the road surface of their own country's highways should be regarded as a guide. All the detailed information collected in various countries will be compiled into a report within a few days and submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the National Economic Commission.

Photo of Xue Cixin arriving in Shanghai (International News Agency)

Regulations of the Ministry of Finance: Measures for Exporting Surplus Salt to Japan 121

Hua Dong News Agency reports that, according to the Salt Affairs Inspection Office, regarding the export of surplus salt from various districts to Japan for use as industrial salt, the Ministry of Finance has now thoroughly reviewed the case. In order to adapt to the current actual situation, four measures are stipulated: 1. If there are surplus salt slices in various districts, they will be allowed to be exported to Japan for use as industrial salt, but only after being certified by the Japanese Monopoly Bureau will they be allowed to be exported to Japan; 2. Merchants in various districts who request export should first submit a written request to the local salt affairs authorities, which will conduct a thorough examination to ensure that they are purely Chinese merchants with substantial capital. The request will be submitted to the headquarters for review and verification, and they will be officially appointed as exporters. Those who submit written requests directly to the headquarters will be ordered to be examined and reported by the competent authorities in each district before being approved. The number of exporters will be fixed at three or more in each district, and a trial will be conducted for one year; 3. The tax rate for industrial salt exported to Japan from various districts will be temporarily set at one yuan per ton, and a cash deposit or a solid bank guarantee should also be levied at the highest tax rate in each district; 4. When salt is exported, all procedures regarding inspection and other matters should still be handled in accordance with the measures for exporting Chinese salt.
