Qingdao Road: Murder Case Occurs, Man and Woman Die Tragically in a Pool of Blood 126

Qingdao Road, under the jurisdiction of the Public Concession's Xinzha Police Station, is located between Xinzha Road and Avenue Edward VII, extending east to Park Road (commonly known as Soy Sauce Alley) and west to Medhurst Road. It is no more than forty or fifty zhang in length. On the south side of the road is a large open space. Last year, Chenxing Lane, a municipal housing complex, was newly built, providing over two hundred rooms. The municipal housing consists of three-story buildings. In the room of the pavilion at No. 51 Qingdao Road (back door leading to No. 39 Chenxing Lane), a bloody incident suddenly occurred. The second landlord, surnamed Wang, is blind and lives on the mezzanine of the first and second floors. He heard the woman surnamed Huang in the pavilion shouting for help and immediately went to check (because the mezzanine where the second landlord lives is opposite the pavilion). He found that the door to the pavilion room was tightly closed, and there was no sound. Therefore, the second landlord immediately ran to report to the Xinzha Police Station, which dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to rush to the scene. They opened the door and saw that both the man and woman were lying in a pool of blood. The man was lying on the bed with his throat cut, and the woman was lying on the cement floor in front of the bed, with six or seven stab wounds on her neck, head, and chest. The police immediately summoned an ambulance and sent the bodies to the morgue for examination. After investigation, it was learned that the deceased had moved in around October of the previous lunar year and had no children or other family members. It is unknown why such a tragedy occurred. However, judging from the situation, it seemed that the tenant surnamed Huang had first stabbed the woman to death and then hanged himself. The second landlord could not determine the exact cause. It was also learned that the house was a three-story single-family building facing north, housing more than ten families, including those surnamed Xue, Chen, and Wei, so the situation was very complicated.

Hangzhou Municipal Government Responds to Zoo: Sends People to Hangzhou to Capture Tiger, to be Assisted by Hangzhou Equestrian and Archery Association 127

At Majia Mountain, four li away from West Lake in Hangzhou, news suddenly emerged that a tiger had attacked and injured a pedestrian. The Municipal Zoo on Temple Road in the city paid close attention to this news. The zoo's original tiger had died of lung disease last year, and it had sent people to Hong Kong to entrust animal dealers to find a tiger in Yunnan and Guizhou, but no deal had been reached. Therefore, the zoo immediately formally wrote to the Hangzhou Municipal Government, asking for permission to capture the tiger if the report was true. It is now learned that the zoo has received a reply from the Hangzhou Municipal Government, requesting the zoo to send people to Hangzhou to capture the tiger and inviting the Hangzhou Equestrian and Archery Association to assist.

Shanghai Weather Clear, Huangpu River Experiences Continuous High Tides, from the 23rd to the 25th, Huangpu River Conservancy Bureau Measures Tidal Volumes 128

After a sudden wind and rain the day before yesterday, the weather cleared up last night. Yesterday, the weather was especially clear and the climate was mild. However, the Huangpu River is experiencing high tides for several consecutive days due to the spring flood season. The Datong News Agency reporter recorded the predicted high tide levels for the Huangpu River from yesterday to the 25th from the Huangpu River Conservancy Bureau. The morning tide yesterday occurred suddenly at 1:17 AM, reaching a height of 10 feet and 9 inches. The afternoon tide occurred suddenly at 1:45 PM, reaching a height of 10 feet and 1.5 inches. The morning tide today is expected to occur at 1:58 AM, reaching a height of 10 feet and 7 inches. The afternoon tide is expected to occur at 2:31 PM, reaching a height of 9 feet and 1 inch. The morning tide on the 25th is expected to occur at 2:15 AM, reaching a height of 10 feet and 0.5 inches. The afternoon tide is expected to occur at 3:20 PM, and the height has receded to below 8 feet, returning to normal.

French Concession Police Capture Large Number of Kidnappers, Bust Three Hideouts, Arrest 21 Male and Female Criminals, Rescue Three Boys and Girls, Two Children Already Trafficked 129

French Concession police detectives Zhang Ziying, Zhou Buguang, Tao Desheng, Jiang Changwen, and detectives Lu Dongbiao, Jin Bingwen, Le Sixiang, Zuo Qihong, etc., busted a large number of kidnappers the day before yesterday. The details are recorded below. Li Qi, a woman from Yangzhou, 30 years old, who lives at No. 246 Dongxin Lane, Jiasiyi Road, in the French Concession, has a four-year-old daughter named Qiaofeng. The day before yesterday, the 21st, at 1:00 PM, Qi's sister-in-law, Zeng, took Qiaofeng to play at the entrance. When Zeng went to the nearby public stove to get water and returned home, Qiaofeng suddenly disappeared. Zeng immediately searched to Xieqiao and saw a woman, Li Zhao, 37 years old, from Anhui, leading Qiaofeng. So she called the police and brought them to the police station. After interrogation by Detective Zhang and others, Zhao confessed that the kidnapping organization was located in a shed at No. 144 Xinxin North Lane, Rue du Père Robert. The detectives went to the address and arrested kidnappers Jin Dianchen, 45 years old, his wife Jin Ge, 43 years old, and Chen Zhang, 27 years old, and Zhang Tao, 46 years old, all from Anhui. At that time, they rescued a five-year-old boy named Dong Zhixiang, who lived at No. 16, Lane 1472, Zengbei Zhonghua Road, the son of Dong Caiming from Haimen. He had been kidnapped on the 20th and brought to the police station together. After questioning Jin Dianchen, he confessed that there were other accomplices hiding at No. 9 to 11 Rulan Lane, Changan Road, Zhabei. The detectives went to Zhabei according to the confession, and together with detectives from the Public Security Bureau, arrested Tang Huijiu, 62 years old, Tang's son Tang Xifu, 21 years old, Lu Lin, 32 years old, Wan Yangzi, 20 years old, Gao Fubao, 13 years old, Pan Chen, 60 years old, Wan Zhang, 63 years old, Gao Zhou, 59 years old, etc. They rescued a kidnapped boy named Shen Axiao, the son of Shen Wang, a local resident of No. 51 Jintong Village, Xujiahui Road, who was kidnapped on April 17th. The criminals also confessed that there was another hideout at No. 41 Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, on the second floor in the front building. They then went to that location and arrested Gao Jiayou, Jin Yuanliang, Jin Li, Jin Shuzhen, Yuan Chen, Chen Xiaomao, Xiao Shao, Gao Chen, and eight others. According to Gao's confession, on March 15th, they kidnapped two boys from the home of Ma Jichang, a beef seller at No. 417 Rue du Père Robert, one named Dayangzi, 6 years old, and one named Sanyangzi, 4 years old. They had been sold to Xiamen and the money had been used. They were taken to the Public Security Bureau for detention. Yesterday afternoon, the French Police Department escorted five criminals, including Li Zhao, to the Second Special Court. The police lawyer stated that the case was still under investigation and requested a postponement for further verification. The victims first described the circumstances of the kidnapping. The defendants' confessions were evasive. Judge Zhang ordered them to be remanded in custody and scheduled another hearing for the 30th.

Drug Den Busted on East Qiu Jiang Road, Three Men and Women Arrested, Mastermind at Large 131

It was discovered that a private drug trafficking organization was operating at No. 109 East Qiu Jiang Road, Zhabei. The Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched An Taidong, along with Peng Shuyuan from the North Sichuan Road Police Station, to lead police to the address. They broke down the door and arrested Zhang Nanping, Zhang Lu, and Qian Jinfa, three men and women, on the spot. They seized evidence such as heroin, red pills, small money boxes, opium pipes, and scrapers. They took the suspects to the bureau for interrogation. The mastermind is at large and is being pursued.

Japanese Sailor Shooting Case: No Political Implications 135

Concession authorities believe it was an ordinary nightclub brawl. The clue to solving the case was obtained from a Little Guangdong who pawned a pistol. A hole in a Western book was found shaped like a pistol.

On the night of November 9th of last year, Zhongshan Xiuxiong, a sailor from the Japanese fleet stationed in Shanghai, was shot and killed by gunfire on North Sichuan Road and Baolean Road. The murderer escaped. The military police authorities of the city and the concession police conducted a thorough investigation and offered a large reward, but six months have passed without any progress. Only this Monday and Tuesday did the Special Political Department of the Public Concession Police Department successively arrest three Chinese people related to the murder and send them to the First Special District Local Court for interrogation. However, both the court and the police department believe that this case is extremely important. During this investigation, absolute secrecy should be maintained, and no procedures should be disclosed to avoid hindering the investigation. Therefore, although the court has held two preliminary hearings, only a few responsible personnel were allowed to attend. The secrecy was unprecedented. Therefore, the various news reports about the solving of the case in the Chinese and foreign newspapers in recent days have been vague. The outside world originally paid close attention to the case, but now the reports are vague, leading to speculation. To avoid causing confusion among the public, we have inquired with a certain party to clarify the actual situation of the solving of the case, and record it as follows. The degree to which the detainees are suspected of being involved in the case will only be clear after a public trial in the future, and cannot be speculated at present.

Investigation Process:

After Zhongshan Xiuxiong's death, the Japanese military headquarters and the Public Concession Police Department sent senior officials to the scene of the incident to investigate. A B.P. brand pistol was found at the scene, proving that this pistol was used to kill Zhongshan Xiuxiong. Later, someone reported to the police that they had seen a person named Little Guangdong pawn a pistol of the same brand with Guangdong native Zeng Yuan for a loan. The police summoned Zeng Yuan, and after examining several pistols, including the one found at the scene, Zeng Yuan took out the one found at the scene, saying that it was Little Guangdong's pawn. Since the loan had been repaid, the gun had been returned to Little Guangdong. Therefore, the police began to investigate Little Guangdong's whereabouts. Initially, there were no clues, so his whereabouts remained unknown for several months. Recently, it was learned that Little Guangdong was in Qingdao, so a few days ago, experienced detectives were selected to go to Qingdao by ship and arrest Little Guangdong. By last Sunday, Little Guangdong had not yet been escorted to Shanghai, but the police had already arrested two Chinese people, A and B, in a certain place. A Western book was found in A's residence, with a hole dug out that was shaped like a pistol. When the found pistol was inserted, it fit perfectly. A was considered to be involved, and B was arrested because of his close relationship with A. On Monday afternoon, the police first sent A and B to the First Special Court, where Judge Xiao Xiefei held two preliminary hearings and ordered them to be remanded in custody. The next morning, Little Guangdong was escorted from Qingdao and sent to the court, where Judge Feng Shide questioned him once and also ordered him to be remanded in custody. It is now heard that the three will be brought to the court for further hearing next Monday.

Reports in Western Newspapers:

According to the Continental Daily, the Public Concession authorities stated yesterday that the shooting death of Japanese sailor Zhongshan Xiuxiong on November 9th of last year had no political motive, but was merely the result of an ordinary brawl in a nightclub. Although the recent developments in this case are still being kept secret, according to personnel who were previously involved in the investigation of this case, their speculation is that the recent arrest of five Chinese people (three men and two women, one of whom is a dancer) shows that the case has no political connection. One of the two women is Chen Guizhen from Ningbo, and the other is Ye Lin from Guangdong. Both were arrested at the Yuegong Dance Hall on Sichuan Road. They will probably be sent to court for questioning this morning. Since the arrest of these two women, the number of suspects arrested in this case has reached six. In addition to the five Chinese people, the other person is a Korean, who was arrested by the police station of the Japanese Consulate in Seoul and is still in the hands of the Japanese authorities. According to news obtained by the Continental Daily yesterday, there will probably be more suspects arrested in this case. It is heard that one of them is closely related to the case and is urgently awaiting capture. It is now believed that this person has fled to Qingdao. According to reliable sources, this person is probably the actual shooter. Yesterday, when officials were asked about the case, they still did not know when the case would be publicly announced or why it was being kept secret. The Japanese authorities, like the concession authorities, have always kept this case secret. When the Continental Daily reporter went to inquire yesterday, they stated that they had forbidden all Japanese newspapers in Shanghai from publishing a single word about it.

Kuang Zhongmou, owner of the Penglai Market, was sued by his stepwife, Kuang Zeng, to the Shanghai Local Court for failure to manage her savings. On the 19th of this month, lawyers Zhang Shizhao, Peng Yuanxun, and Liu Guangyue visited Zeng at the Kuang residence to discuss reconciliation, but the reconciliation failed because Kuang's wife's conditions were too harsh. The lawyers drafted a record of the mediation and submitted it to the court for review. The reporter obtained the mediation record from lawyer Zhang Shizhao, which is summarized below: On the 19th of this month, the husband's lawyers, Zhang, Peng, and Liu, went to Kuang Lu at No. 88 Hejia Lane, Shangwen Road, to meet with Kuang Zeng and discuss reconciliation. Lawyer Zhang said first, "Mr. Kuang and Madam Kuang, we are here today under the court's order to mediate your marital lawsuit. As lawyers appointed by the court and responsible for mediation, it is our duty to make efforts. I think you have been married for many years and have many children. Why have disagreements? If you are determined to pursue the lawsuit, I would like to ask you to express a peaceful resolution and at the same time persuade Mr. Kuang to provide you with adequate financial compensation. As you know, during the existence of the marital relationship, the husband manages the joint property of the husband and wife according to law." Zeng replied, "I am afraid that it is not something that a few of you lawyers can discuss well. Our lawsuit has already reached this point." Lawyer Zhang said, "As long as there is sincerity and both parties do not insist on their own opinions, there is no reason why it cannot be discussed well. Please, Madam Kuang, propose your conditions so that we can all discuss them." Zeng then proposed the following conditions: 1. Mr. Kuang must be held responsible for canceling the marriage between his second son, Baozhen, and Cheng Meifang, and selecting a lady of equal status to his eldest son, Baoying's wife, for a remarriage. 2. Mr. Kuang must be held responsible for calling Xiao Tianbao, the inspector of the Penglai Market, to come before me, kneel down in front of me, and let me beat him to death alive. Mr. Kuang will be responsible for the consequences. 3. If Mr. Kuang wants to come back, he must give me a written statement in advance (i.e., write a confession) guaranteeing that he will no longer live outside and do other things that I consider wrong. 4. All of Mr. Kuang's property and economic rights must be completely handed over to me for joint management. I will manage all household expenses. Zeng also said, "If the above four conditions can be met, come and talk to me again. If they cannot be met, there is no need to come back."

Zhang Yuanruo Discusses the Constitution Implementation Problem: His Early Advocacy for Adding Transitional Clauses; Implementing Constitutionalism is Key to China's Order and Disorder; Distribution and Implementation Should be Treated as Two Separate Issues; Difficulties in Implementation Should be Considered Before Promulgation 140

Regarding the issue of revising the draft constitution, central government figures have recently held frequent meetings, attracting considerable attention from various quarters. A reporter specially visited Mr. Zhang Yuanruo, a constitutional scholar and secretary of the municipal government, at his residence, and he shared his views on the issue of implementing constitutional government. His words were quite insightful, and are recorded as follows:

Mr. Zhang briefly stated that he had been paying attention to the issue of promulgating and implementing a constitution for some time. Last May, he drafted a special article published in major newspapers in response to Mr. Wu Jingxiong, the vice-chairman of the Constitution Drafting Committee, regarding how the constitution should be implemented and how temporary clauses should be established to seek remedies. He listed historical facts and specific clauses from the constitutional history of various countries and offered them to the authorities. Although his ideas were greatly appreciated in theory at the time, they were not adopted in practice. Now that Mr. Wang Liangchou has returned from overseas and the authorities are paying attention to this, I am deeply gratified.

Implementing constitutionalism is indeed an essential plan for a country's long-term stability and security. However, if implementation is not done properly, it can also lead to sources of turmoil. Since the founding of the Republic, the political situation has been turbulent, and the source of these troubles can invariably be traced back to constitutional issues. Therefore, the implementation of constitutionalism is a crucial key to China's order and disorder. Past events are a clear lesson.

In the past, the common ailment of those who discussed the constitution in our country was that they only paid attention to the "form" of the constitution and did not pay attention to its "use." They only engaged in the "dead" imitation of the clauses and did not emphasize the "living" application of constitutionalism. They did not understand that a constitution is a product of history and a reflection of the actual life of a nation. It cannot "walk on its own" and cannot be implemented effectively simply by being arbitrarily formulated. Therefore, the heart of today's constitutional problem lies not in the establishment and detail of the constitutional text and format, but in the flexibility and effectiveness of constitutional application. Now that the draft constitution has been finalized, of course it must be promulgated, but promulgation is one thing, and implementation is another. They should not be confused. If, in the process of promulgation and implementation, we can urgently seek sound transitional measures, then it will be like mending the fold after the sheep is lost, and things can still be done. Otherwise, if we leap over the necessary stages of historical evolution, and if implementation is ineffective or flawed, the ensuing turmoil will be unimaginable.

Upon investigation, the Founding Outline and the arrangements for the publication and implementation of the constitution were quite prudent. One stated: "The draft constitution should be based on the Founding Outline and the achievements of both the tutelage and constitutional periods, and be deliberated by the Legislative Yuan, and publicized to the people at any time, in order to be selected and implemented when the time comes." The other stated: "When more than half of the provinces in the country have reached the constitutional period, that is, the period when provincial autonomy is fully established, a National Assembly shall be convened to decide on the constitution and promulgate it." According to the latter statement, the promulgation of the constitution and the convening of the National Assembly should both be premised on the completion of local self-government. According to the former statement, the deliberation of the constitution should be based on the actual achievements of political tutelage, and the implementation of the constitution should wait for a considerable period of time.

This kind of approach is in line with the national conditions. Considering the norms and realities of constitutional government in various countries around the world, it is also not wrong. For example, in Finland and Poland, the implementation of their constitutions is separately regulated by law. In Siam, although the constitution is implemented from the date of promulgation, it is subject to temporary provisions. In Lithuania, the implementation of the constitution must be approved by a national referendum within ten years. In Prussia, only Articles 31-43 and 86 of the constitution became effective after promulgation; the remaining articles should be implemented after the new elections are completed. Even in England and France, the models of constitutional government, the implementation of the constitution was initially limited to a certain part, and was later supplemented and gradually perfected. The Chinese people's political capacity is still very weak, and the work of political tutelage is largely incomplete. At this time, the constitution must not only seek the completeness of the clauses, but also consider the various difficulties in practical application. All experienced statesmen should strive to avoid politeness, not sing high-sounding tunes, and seek a sound remedy for China's constitutional government. It is said that Mr. Zhang will have time in the next few days, and may draft another special article to contribute to the authorities.

Jin Youshan's Wife, Pan Jingwen, Proved by Forensic Doctor to Have No Mental Illness; The Prescriptions Opened by the Mental Hospital Were Still Appropriate; After Yesterday's Court Trial, Sentencing is Scheduled for Tomorrow 141

The Shanghai Mental Hospital on 888 Kangning Road, Shanghai, was founded by Gu Wensi and has been in operation for several years. Two Major New Developments in Transportation 148

Tasmania, 180 miles from Australia, has been connected to the world by telephone since the installation of an undersea telephone line was completed on March 25. This cable is one of the world's largest undersea telephone cables, with six loop currents and many telegraph lines, as well as special lines for radio broadcasting. All companies related to the International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation of the UK and Australia participated in the project and equipment. At the opening, the Australian Director-General of Transport, Mr. Blanc, spoke with Mr. Payne, President of the New York International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation, from Better, Tasmania. The island has about 16,000 telephones. The communication of Anglo-American wireless telegraph was first tested by the Queen Mary on March 25 when it sailed through the Kleret River. Telegraphs were sent from the ship and received by the Mackay Wireless Telegraph Company station in Sansaunton. The wireless radio installed on the Queen Mary is the greatest equipment in recent years. Its machinery is complete and is a two-way wireless telephone and telegraph, which can communicate with European and American countries during the voyage. The supplier of the machinery is the London International Marine Radio Company, also an affiliated company of the International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation.

Ms. Yang Lingfu of Wuxi is fluent in English, French, Russian, and Japanese, and is skilled in the arts. She is excellent in poetry, calligraphy, and painting. She once copied 96 portraits of emperors of past dynasties in the Forbidden City and 25 portraits of emperors and empresses of the Qing Dynasty. New Development of China Oil Lamp Company 159

China Oil Lamp Company at 218 Shandong Road in this city specializes in manufacturing and selling plant oil lamps invented by Zhong. They are well-constructed and have beautiful styles. All kinds of plant oils produced in our country, such as rapeseed oil, cottonseed oil, peanut oil, sesame oil, tung oil, tea oil, and cypress oil, can be burned. They emit bright light, better than kerosene lamps, without any smoke toxicity, and avoid fires. They can be said to be safe and hygienic, and also save oil (taking the local rapeseed oil as a standard, each four hours consumes the national currency one cent), which is in line with the needs of the general public in inland cities, towns, and villages. They have been tested by the Military Affairs Committee's camp, proving that they are indeed superior and economical to kerosene lamps, and have ordered their subordinate units to purchase them together. They have also been approved by the local governments of various provinces to be exempt from tax for sale. The company, due to the advent of oil lamps, plant oil has suddenly added a large sales channel, and is deeply afraid of affecting the original use, and has repeatedly approved the Ministry of Industry and the National Economic Commission to issue a notice to the country, widely planting seedling oil. The Ministry of Industry also sent letters to the construction departments of various provinces across the country, ordering the road management agencies to plant cypress trees along the roads to extract fuel. Recently, they have re-submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, ordering the Ministry of Interior and the National Economic Committee to issue a notice to the country, ordering that sesame be planted first on newly reclaimed land to enrich oil production. They have also obtained assistance from the China Agricultural Loan Group, which is composed of major banks, and the Anhui Provincial Local Bank to carry out oil seedling loans in various places. It is heard that the Jiangsu Farmers Bank has sent personnel to contact the company to discuss the issue of oil seedling loans, and a specific method has been determined, which will be implemented soon. In addition, the company's wind and rain lamps will be shipped next month. They are of excellent quality and beautiful style. The Chinese oil stove is also in the design and manufacture.

Sales Reservation of "Gold Coffer Revealing the Mysteries" 161

Cao Yingfu of Jiangyin is a veteran in the field of traditional Chinese medicine and has served as the director of teaching affairs at the Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine College. He has devoted his life to the study of Zhongjing's learning, taking the "Treatise on Cold Damage" as the golden rule for treating diseases throughout the ages. Based on his 40 years of medical research and past clinical experience, he wrote the book "Revealing the Mysteries of Cold Damage," which has been widely acclaimed in the medical field. He also believes that Zhongjing's "Synopsis of the Golden Chamber" is actually intertwined with the "Treatise on Cold Damage" and is a book that must be read by those who study medicine. However, there are errors in transmission and writing, and there have been few successors since Xu You. The meaning is hidden and obscure, and practitioners suffer from it. Therefore, following the example of annotating the "Treatise on Cold Damage", he wrote the book "Gold Coffer Revealing the Mysteries" to correct errors, reveal the essence, and add clinical experience from previous years to each prescription, making the book "Gold Coffer" clear, transparent, and convenient for scholars. It is by no means superficial. Ding Jiwan, Bo Wei, Yi Ren, Xu Banlong, Chen Cunren and others have specially proofread and published it. The actual price of each book is three yuan, the reservation price is one yuan and five dimes, the deadline is the end of May. If you purchase it together with "Revealing the Mysteries of Cold Damage" during the reservation, you will only be charged half the original price, two yuan. The postage for each book to other places is two dimes and four cents. The reservation office is the Medical Bookstore at No. 204 Mayberg Road, Shanghai.

The Insurance Industry in Shanghai Edited by China Credit Reporting (An Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce - 23) 165

Among the above-mentioned Chinese-owned insurance companies, the largest in terms of capital and scale are Taiping Insurance Company, Tianyi Insurance Company, and China Insurance Company. The situations of each company are described below.

1. Taiping Insurance Company: This company was founded in the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929), with a total capital of 5 million yuan and a paid-up capital of 3 million yuan. Various reserves totaled 2,678,13.05 yuan by the end of the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934). The chairman is Huang Yizhu, the executive directors are Hu Bijiang, Xu Hanqing, Tang Shoumin, Qian Xinzhi, and Zhou Zuomin, and the general manager is Zhou Zuomin. Its shareholders are six banks: Jiaotong, Dalu, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, Guohua, and Donglai. The head office is located at No. 212 Jiangxi Road, with branches in Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, Guangzhou, Jinan, Zhengzhou, and other places. There are over 290 agencies, covering almost all major cities in the country. Anping and Fengsheng are also affiliated companies. The annual premium income is 700,000 to 800,000 yuan, and the annual profit is 300,000 to 400,000 yuan. The fire insurance business is the most developed.

2. Tianyi Insurance Company: This company was founded in the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934), with a total capital of 5 million yuan and a paid-up capital of 2.5 million yuan. The chairman is Wang Boyuan, the directors are He Gusheng, Run Qing, Hu Wenhu, Wang Zisong, Liang Nonglan, Qian Xinzhi, Zhu Yinjiang, and Huang Zhongchang, and the general manager is Liang Chenlan. Its shareholders are all important staff members of the industry bank. The head office is located at No. 255 Beijing Road, Shanghai, with branches in Shanghai, Nanjing, Tianjin, Hankou, Qingdao, Ningbo, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Beiping, and other places. Agencies are located throughout the country. Although its annual premium income is not specified, it is not much different from that of Taiping Insurance Company.

3. China Insurance Company: This company was founded in the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931), with an authorized capital of 5 million yuan and a paid-up capital of 2.5 million yuan. By the end of the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1934), various public reserves totaled 675,505.76 yuan, and various reserve funds totaled 426,453.02 yuan. The chairman is Song Hanzhang, the executive directors are Song Ziwen, Bei Songsun, Zhang Gongquan, and Wang Lengbo, and the manager is Guo Fuyun. The head office is located at No. 270 Sichuan Road, Shanghai, with agencies throughout the country. Its business policy is extremely prudent. It does not underwrite insurance with greater risks. The fire insurance business is relatively developed.

The original plan for this first batch of representatives to come to Shanghai was to take the Longtian Maru to facilitate their participation in the three matches in Shanghai. However, due to misunderstandings in various circles in Hong Kong, the ride was canceled. Fortunately, the German wheel Boston opened late, so the team members were able to catch the wheel to Shanghai. I will not be able to participate in the matches in Shanghai. As for the lineup for the matches in Shanghai, in order for the people of Shanghai to appreciate the talents of the southern players, Jia Youliang, the representative selected from this city, will not play. When the representative team goes abroad, the matches in Nanyang, Saigon, Medan, and Java have been arranged. The rest are still being negotiated, he said.

The pre-selection events for the 8th Elementary School Joint Sports Meet in the districts of Lixing, Gaoqiao, Xiaojing, and Yangsi have already been reported in yesterday's newspaper. The following is a continuation of the news from the districts of Yangjing, Tangqiao, Jiangyin, and Gaoxing:

Yangjing: The Yangjing District pre-selection committee held its first preparatory meeting yesterday at the Municipal Zhenxiu Elementary School. The following resolutions were made: The date for the pre-selection meet is set for April 28th, with postponement in case of rain. The venue will be the playground of the Municipal Yangjing Elementary School. The organizing committee will be divided into a general affairs department and a sports department. The expenses will be shared by the schools, tentatively calculated at four yuan per class, to be prepaid at the time of registration. The registration deadline is 6:00 PM on April 26th. In addition to the physical education teachers from each school, nine additional judges will be hired. The quota of representatives from this district will not be determined for the time being. After the pre-selection meet, the best candidates will be selected to participate in the main event. The badges will be distributed before 8:00 AM on April 28th. Pins are to be provided by the participants themselves.

It was decided that the selection of representatives from this district to attend the main event will be held on Wednesday, April 29th, at the Pudong Middle School sports field.

Jiangyin: The Jiangyin District pre-selection committee held its first preparatory meeting yesterday afternoon at the Qiujiang Elementary School. Job assignments were allocated: Qiujiang, Zhongshan, and Lingnan for competitions; Fudan Yixiao and Liangjiang for social affairs; Yinxi for discipline. The office will be located at Qiujiang Elementary School, behind Jiangwan Dasi. Registration for each school will be open from now until the 28th.

Gaoxing: The Gaoxing District pre-selection committee held its first preparatory meeting yesterday. Those present were Zhang Chengxiu, Ling Yaohan, Qu Zhixu, Qu Xing, and Zhang Meiting. Zhang Chengxiu chaired the meeting, and Ling Yaohan recorded the minutes. The following resolutions were made: Job assignments were allocated: Zhang Chengxiu for general affairs, Ling Yaohan for social affairs, Zhang Meiting for discipline, Qu Zhixu for statistics, and Qu Xing for prize collection. The date for the pre-selection meet is set for 9:00 AM on May 2nd (with postponement in case of rain). The venue will be the playground of Gaoxing Elementary School. Commercial News

Finance Silver Price Drops, Gold Rises; Call Money Only Rises Half a Yuan 197

The gold market was stable yesterday, then gradually flattened. People's hearts were unsettled. The silver market declined, pure gold rose, and large investors' buying interest was relatively strong, resulting in a slight increase. The foreign exchange market turned flat, with a rather stable trend. Early in the morning, the overseas silver market showed declines in both the UK and the US. Brokers said that the market situation would stabilize after the close. India was buying at the listed price, and at the close, there were sellers at the listed price plus 0.0625. Mont de Piété forward silver prices were unchanged or down by up to half a cent. Exchange rates all declined. London spot gold rose by 1.5 pence. The Central Bank announced its listed prices, with both the UK and the US unchanged, and the Customs Gold Unit unchanged. The standard gold price was listed at 1145.9 yuan, and off-exchange forward trading opened at 44 to 44.5 yuan. Qingfa, Yongfu, and Dafuxing Yong took advantage of the high price to offer call options and retreated to within 4 yuan. Dadecheng bought strongly and stabilized. Shenbao Literary Supplement

Enchantment 220

— Cao Ming

It wasn't even a few hours since Fourth Sister, who people called "Thief Woman," returned to her village when everyone knew.

Her face, plump and vigorous like a bun, her stout body, and the silk clothes, gold bracelets, watch, and real stone rings incongruously adorning her, had appeared so often in people's eyes that their intense curiosity slowly faded. Though the women still acted warmly towards her when they met, appearing to listen intently to her lengthy words mixed with incorrect provincial accents and newfangled terms.

I hadn't forgotten the last time Fourth Sister returned home. One of my distant aunts, with many frivolous words and excessive laughter, kept Fourth Sister company for over half an hour. But as Fourth Sister turned to leave, she pursed her lips and said with utter contempt:

"That free woman, hmm, that thief woman, could she even raise a son with a bottom? The things she wears, I wonder from whose house she stole them…"

I asked my aunt at the time: "But weren't you just acting differently towards her?"

Offended by my question, she didn't answer. She just turned back and widened her eyes as she left, saying:

"Let me tell you, this is teaching you how to behave!"

I ran into Fourth Sister on the third morning after her return.

"Let's go have tea, let's go to Shun Yu Lou for tea," she urged. Her short, sturdy figure leaned against the iron railing of Wenlan Bridge. The morning breeze ruffled her carelessly styled hair; her arms, though short, moved nimbly; her speech was filled with a shallow boldness. Combining all her bold, brash, fierce, childlike straightforwardness— such a character was hard to find in the village. The urgency of her speech, the restless darting of her eyes, and the agile turning of her head and hands all showed that she was accustomed to that kind of adventurous, fluid life.

"There are a lot of men there," I disagreed.

"Forget it, what's the big deal! Even a schoolgirl acts so prissy. My son is a man too," she said, laughing loudly and slapping my shoulder hard. According to her, she puffed out her chest, swinging her arms, her face as if facing a close friend every minute, and bought a big bag of buns from Shunxing Lou and came back.

We crossed Wenlan Bridge and entered Qili Pavilion, across from the mulberry fields. She ate and spoke non-stop, saying things that tasted like nothing to me. Later, she changed her approach, pointing to her gold jewelry, explaining in detail which styles were now the most popular in Shanghai, and which stones were worth more than others.

"Alas, I'm still missing a top-quality diamond, I love it the most! What about you, what do you love the most? Let's talk about what I'm wearing."

"None of this can bring you glory. The whole village looks down on you!"

The sun revealed half its body, and the surroundings slowly became hot. The mulberry trees gently trembled, bracing themselves to resist the sun's fiery power. I felt uneasy; what should I say to Fourth Sister at this moment? She didn't seem to understand what I said; she looked at me and laughed loudly. After a long silence, she defended herself:

"When I worked in the silk factory, no one ever looked up to me either. People seemed to never have time to talk to me!—But now they actually… Alas, did I steal these things for nothing?" She played with her ornaments again, just like a child with their toys, not out of necessity but for pleasure.

Her stubbornness annoyed me, so I simplified my meaning and said, "I'm talking about a person's character! If a person's soul is stained, then even gold plating cannot hide it!"

"Oh, character, right, I also heard that term when I was in the provincial capital. Ah Ming, you've been to school for two years, so maybe you understand more; but since a person ultimately has to eat, in this world, as long as you show your courage, show your strength, and show your ideas, then isn't he a person of character? Hmm, character is not like money, hidden away by people; whoever wants it can just take it, I won't wait for others to give it to me, nor will I steal it from others, right, haha…" To explain her point, her hands and features became even more active, talking non-stop, as if not willing to relax my attention for a moment. "It's all just about the problem of eating. What's the difference?—Picking mulberry leaves, sorting cocoons, reeling silk, being a prostitute, being a robber… You name it, you pick out one of these careers that is more noble! You know, a person often encounters times when 'you're not allowed to choose.' …As for tomorrow, I don't care about that, I don't even know what morality or law is; even knowing that I'll kick the bucket tomorrow, I'm not willing to starve today! I only know that I want to live, I only know that I want to find a bowl of rice to eat!…" Her buttocks suddenly left the stone stool, and she jumped around in the pavilion, yelling.

She looked a bit excited, but she was always so cheerful and confident, as if there was nothing terrible or scary in her mind. She still jumped around anxiously, like an ant on a hot pot, constantly cursing the hot weather, and using her hand as a fan.

"Only knowing how to live—that's right, but you should know how to live properly. Some ways of living will destroy our souls…!"

She seemed unwilling for me to continue, interrupting me with her words.

"Hey, you're about to become a female teacher, right? But I'm not even qualified to be your student. How can I get through such hot weather? I've only been back for two days, and I'm already getting bored again, I can't live such a stable life anymore. I'm going back to Tengchong tomorrow, maybe even today, alas!…"

For some small reason, she left Qili Pavilion like a grasshopper. I stayed in the pavilion alone for a long time, thinking about this enchanting woman.

"In the Beginning was the Deed" 221

— Li Bo

—Thoughts after Reading Goethe's "Faust"—

In his study, Doctor Faust, "yearning for life's rivers, desperately longing for life's source," was again struggling with the anxieties of life's thirst. To remedy the emptiness and deficiencies in his life, he opened the Hebrew Bible, hoping to find some "noble and beautiful" revelations within. He translated the phrase "In the beginning was the Word," but felt that the word "Word" was unclear, and translated it again as "In the beginning was the Mind." But "Mind" cannot create the universe, so he finally decided to write it as "In the beginning was the Power." Still feeling it was inappropriate, he finally, with "divine penmanship," translated the first sentence of the "Gospel of John" as "In the beginning was the Deed" (In the beginning was the deed). He laughed with joy.

Regardless of how "Faust" develops later, this is truly a "noble and beautiful" revelation.

What will not fade with time are the books written by life. The most valuable are the words containing actions, that is, the words accumulated from actions. In the world, there are many literati who idly play with words behind colored gauze windows, and there are also pedantic scholars who spend their entire lives caressing dwarf corruptions detached from life and gleefully congratulating themselves, but when they see the dazzling light of life, they will all turn withered or pale.

Knowing a few words can also allow one to learn some practical theories and copy fragments of ideologies. But when the storms of life arrive, it will make people feel regret even more. The ideologies that were originally foreign to his life will be buried or ruined by him; the progress of his life will ultimately follow his own animal-level interests and psychology. And that second-handed ideology will reveal the flaws between it and life, or even be completely abandoned, or, like a faded fallen leaf in a strong wind, detached from the branch of life, still trying to struggle in mid-air, but will eventually drift into some muddy swamp.

Moreover, even fragmentary parroting and artificial patching are not easy. Besides pure theory, how many prejudices and biases might be inherited! What best disinfects all these toxins, other than action? This society is full of lies. What do we use to prevent the spread of lies, other than action?

The value of theory lies in the fact that it extracts and organizes the experiences of human behavior in the historical movement of reality, and then acts upon the historical movement of reality again. The historical movement of reality is subtle and ever-changing. Once theory leaves it, it will make mistakes, or even become empty and useless.

The civilization of modern European bourgeois society has nurtured writers like James Joyce and Marcel Proust. Joyce's eyes are always fixed on the many dung heaps of human reality. His works have only so many vulgar photos, without any poetic temperament. The great realist Balzac seemed to have said that being able to discover the poetic elements in reality is half of a person's genius. However, in the declining bourgeois society, it is impossible to produce this kind of genius with poetic temperament. Marcel Proust lies in a magnificent salon, looking at the ceiling every day. What does he write? The ceiling is the same every day? How monotonous and tasteless his reality is. Thus, we see another deformed phenomenon in modern literature: next to the ever-changing social reality, there are gentlemen like Proust who are too full, avoiding reality and emanating a pitiful "whisper of dreams" (Gorky's words).

Goethe, an artistic thinker, once pointed out that literature should be a mixture of poetry and truth. Bourgeois society cannot produce great poets, nor does it have faithful authors who depict the social reality truthfully. The analysis of dung and the "whisper of dreams" have become the great boast of their entire literature.

Our country's realists have had an inextricable connection with social movements from the very beginning. However, at present, a part of the literati seems to have a vague tendency to be tired of social life and to despise the current actual movement of the entire nation. What is the future of this tendency? Our country does not even have the conditions for producing the art of Proust and Joyce. If there are people who have the same tendency as their empty lives, then he will, at most, become an unsuccessful Proust, or a weaker and smaller Joyce.

We demand writers with rich knowledge of reality and an exciting spirit of poetry. We demand that writers, for the sake of their own artistic achievement, and also for the sake of the Chinese nation and its cultural future, more passionately love and penetrate the current struggling reality movement. We must follow Hegel's immortal instruction: To have the greatest concern for world history, for the entire society. Our theme should be the necessary action of the world and humanity described under this concern.

All great writers are like this. They experience rich practical life, and love it passionately all their lives. Gorky, Barbusse, Romain Rolland, Gide, their joys and sorrows are mostly the expression of social emotions that care about human history, and their intellect is the intellect of a warrior in the historical movement.

All great theorists are constantly washing their theories on the torrent of the reality movement. This guarantees that their theories will always be fresh, healthy, rich, and powerful. "Let the storm and rain blow more fiercely!" Our greatest poet wrote the famous lines of poetry. How passionately did that genius theorist repeatedly savor them, when he was writing brilliant guiding theories.

Now the storm and rain of the Chinese nation's people's liberation is already fierce enough. What an opportune time for us, writers and theorists! Let us also sing the song of the flying birds welcoming the wind and rain! Or let us bring up the verse of the erudite Faust who admired life:

I think that this is what it means to be a happy person,

Or to die on the battlefield wearing a crown stained with blood,

Or to hold a girl in one's arms after the dance,

If our girls are also about to become slaves, then we will more decisively love the first two lines of poetry, right?

Bugle 222

— Xi Jin

Listen to the sound of the bugle,

That mournful, melancholic tune,

Has turned into a majestic and resounding call.

Come, let us die for survival!

It is our bugle that sounds,

Echoing in the distance and nearby,

Carried by the wind, broadcast to the world.

It will blow straight from the dark night until dawn.

Bandit 223

— Wang Renshu

A desolate road suddenly became lively. The sidewalk outside the Tiancheng Printing House was crowded with men and women of various appearances.

Everyone seemed lost and bewildered: their sallow and gloomy faces, thick black eyebrows covered in ash, bright, green-tinged eyes, and purplish-gray lips that moved slightly, as if wanting to say something but not quite managing it.

"Oh! Huh!"

Someone sighed, as if understanding what was happening. Others immediately followed suit, yawning one after another, as if infected:

"Oh! Huh!"

The central door of the Tiancheng Printing House was open, but the shutters on the glass windows on either side had not yet been removed. People poured in like a black current through the doorway. The small printing room had a counter on the left and a lithographic press on the right. Against the back wall was a bed. It was all extremely simple. No one could tell who the owner was, and they glared at each other with green eyes. Only a middle-aged woman, with a pale, gourd-shaped face, stood facing outward in front of the bed. So, everyone squeezing inside focused their gaze on her, but brought their mouths close to the ears of strangers, looking at the grime behind their ears, smelling the oily odor of their hair, and asking each other, "What's going on?"

Before they could finish speaking, it seemed someone leaned in close, as if listening to mosquitoes buzzing while lying in bed: "Stole…stole…"

A woman immediately blushed red. She scratched her short-cropped hair, looking at the woman standing in front of the bed. She thought, "What could a woman steal?" Her whole body felt hot. She looked at the woman again, and her face strangely transformed into the face of that lovely man she had secretly met behind her husband's back. She thought, "People are really strange things. Which woman is ever completely satisfied with her husband for a lifetime? Who hasn't done something immoral!" "Ugh!" So, as if to calm herself, she coughed once. "Why—why is everyone so crowded!" she cried again, elbowing someone in the stomach, trying to push her way out.

The person she hit was a large man. His pumpkin-like face and fat neck trembled from the impact. He looked at the shouting woman, whose square, blocky ears were adorned with earrings. "Damn!" he thought. "Pretty good lookin'. Just yesterday, used my wife's old earrings to pawn, ate a bellyful of good food, came home and my wife was half-dead from crying and raising hell: shouting 'thief!' and 'you old devil! How could you steal even the last bit of my property!' Damn it! That stupid woman doesn't know how valuable money is these days. There are foreigners who collect silver; if I pawn things now, I can drink even more!" "Heh heh heh! If the world doesn't let me drink yellow wine, how else am I supposed to live?..." And then a line of drool ran down the big man's mouth. Following this, he sneezed: "Ah choo!"

"What's wrong?" A pretty female student turned her face. Her eyebrows were finely drawn in a gentle curve and her rosy cheeks were dusted with a large patch of waxy rouge. She tugged at the arm of her Western-suited male classmate, feigning a look of being bullied. "Let's go out! Let's go out!" But the man, with his messy long hair, looked at the gourd-faced woman through his glasses as if an artist sketching a model, ignoring the female student's urging. The woman grew angry, pouting her delicate little mouth, wriggled her buttocks through the tightly packed legs, and forced her way out, as if muttering to herself, "You old thief! You knew how to steal my kisses in the park, but now you are so absorbed looking at that gourd-face, are you planning to steal her love?"

The man suddenly felt a space open up on his left. He turned to see a head that looked like a bird’s nest, moving outward through the crowd. He immediately turned around within the forest of legs, tracking and catching up in a straight line, completely disregarding the astonished faces to his left and right and the voices near his ears asking "What was stolen? Who’s the thief?", his eyes fixed intently on that bird’s nest head. Once outside on the sidewalk, he grabbed the female student’s left arm and asked, “What’s wrong?”

“What’s wrong?” the woman turned her left corner of her mouth upward. “Someone sneezed on the back of my head and you didn’t even notice!” But then, feeling the warmth of the man’s hand holding her left arm, she changed her mind, asking in an angry tone: "What exactly was stolen?"

"Maybe a man, maybe something else! Who cares!" the man said in a tender tone. Then, he suddenly remembered that he was a university student, and added, "Even our land has been stolen, thousands of miles of it! We can't even control that. Why are we even bothering to worry about a petty thief!" As he spoke, he pushed aside the groups of people gathered on the sidewalk, and walked south, arm in arm.

A policeman in a white hat came towards them. He seemed to have overheard some of what the university student had said. When he reached the entrance of the Tiancheng Printing House, he waved his hands, dispersing the crowd. But as he did so, he also spoke to the crowd, as if telling them not to leave and to listen to his explanation.

"What's so interesting here? The thief has already been caught. It’s a boss and his two employees. —Look! Look! They stole rice from that rice shop!" As he spoke, the hand dispersing the crowd pointed to a small rice shop across the street.

In the crowd, a skinny, short man with an oily face used his greasy, blackened apron to wipe the sweat that had suddenly broken out on his forehead. "Rice! Rice! Oh, damn it! The rice shop owner's rice should be stolen. We restaurant owners suffer because they raise rice prices. If—if—I had known he could steal rice, then, we could have gotten some cheap goods, being on the same street—"

"Stole eleven bags—stole eleven bags!" the policeman continued relentlessly. He seemed to have become interested in the rice theft; he completely sympathized with the thief's superior technique. He said, "Think about it, there are plenty of us patrolling on this street, and he still managed to break in and steal eleven bags! People will hear this and think he's working with us! —Hmm! —Cough!" As he spoke, he suddenly coughed in embarrassment. At this moment, the people inside and outside the door began to mingle. Those who knew it was about stolen rice all felt a little regret in their hearts: "How did he get caught? Alas! If I could have gotten a bag, that would have been so good!"

"Ha! That's really a big thief! Really talented!" someone immediately said, talking about the rice. The words showed praise. But he felt that what he said was improper, and so he added criticism. "Damn it! Shameless! And he's the owner of a printing house?"

"Yes! He's the owner of a printing house!" the policeman, feeling remorseful, immediately corrected himself. He now stood in the middle of the crowd, showing his air of being an expert in catching thieves. "If he specialized in this kind of thing, then people might say, 'Oh! The theft from the rice shop on this street was arranged beforehand with the police!' But he's the owner of a printing house!..."

"Then, then—" a little old woman, lifting her face, displaying a spirit of "dedication to the utmost, until death," asked with great disappointment: "The thief...taken to the station! What about the rice? Where did the rice go! Is it still here... here..." As she spoke, her two damaged eyes looked around, seemingly unable to let go of the crowd-filled doorway. "Alas!" she sighed, "Working hard on the streets all day, without even a measure of rice!"

The heroes of mankind, however, all echoed the policeman's arguments and even praised him:

"That's right! Old fellow! You have talent! If everyone on the same street was stealing from each other, what would become of us! Shanghai is a strange place, a boss stealing rice! Even if the printing business isn't doing well, he can change to another business! -- Hmph!" Then, an invisible bullet was fired from his nose, as if it had hit the thief in the chest, causing him pain.

"But, but—the rice shop owner! Hmm!" the restaurant owner continued to wipe his forehead, saying in a low voice, "The rice shop owner raises rice prices! Hmm! Hmm!..."

"Where? Where? They should lower grain prices even more!" Following this, a voice sounded in the restaurant owner's ear. The owner turned to look: it was a worker from the Rencheng Coal Shop, his black face and hands making him look like a black ghost. "—I, I, was still farming in the countryside last year!"

"Damn it!" But the owner was still thinking about his own affairs. "Even your family's firewood! Hmph!" He glanced at him with his eyes, and then looked at the hero of heroes, the police officer: the police officer was still enthusiastically carrying out his explanation. He wanted to see expressions of praise on every astonished face.

The young women seemed to have put down a load, looking at each other, winking, and pursing their lips, silently exchanging their meanings, as if all felt some joy, but also some sense of lack. They had no time to see the thief's face. They finally asked each other, "What kind of person is he? Thick eyebrows and big eyes? —But he must have a sturdy arm!" An arm, that is what they worshiped, a brave man. A man who could carry eleven bags of rice, flying over walls and roofs—such a man would be so lovely! They turned their heads again, looking into the doorway. They seemed to be jealous of the gourd-faced man standing in front of the bed.

"Go! Go!" The policeman still raised his hand for maintaining order. "What is there to see? The thief has been caught! The stolen goods have been recovered! What is there to see! Go! Go!" And so, an eagle claw-like iron hand flew over the heads of the crowd. The crowd had no intention of leaving: you looked at me, I looked at you, their feet constantly tapping on the same spot.

The eagle claw-like iron hand soared over the head of a thin, yellow-faced young writer. He sighed and said:

"Who exactly is the thief? —Who remembers our land? Who remembers the sweat and blood of the farmers who toil on our land?..."

But in the end, he also stole this subject matter and left.

On the Coast 224

— Shi Dai

—One of the Scenes of Weihaiwei—

The sea wind roared all night long, the cold violently agitating on the shore. The dried yellow fish, hung under the eaves and dried since summer, was slapped against the wall by the wind, making continuous *ba-la ba-la* sounds. After the donkey in the eastern neighbor's yard brayed, the snoring old sow also cried out, rubbed her itchy body against the edge of the trough, and then fell back into her sty, sleeping with a *hu-la hu-la* sound.

When the rooster crowed for the first time, the horse in the neighbor's stable whinnied. At this time, Sister-in-law Shuangxi woke up. She gently touched Fuer next to her. He was sleeping soundly and sweetly. She pulled the quilt over her body up a little more and covered the child tightly. Then, she turned over to push Brother Shuangxi.

"Get up, get up, it's early!"

Brother Shuangxi hummed a couple of times, lazily turned over like a child, and fell asleep again with a snore.

She knew that Brother Shuangxi worked hard all day. Sleeping a little longer was not laziness. He needed to release the fatigue in his body, but his life would not allow him to rest. His child and wife needed him to put food on the table. If he didn't go fishing for even a day, life would give him a hard time. So she had to knock on Brother Shuangxi's back a second time. He yawned a few times, got up, rubbed the sleep from his eyes, and busied himself with putting on his clothes. Finally, he reached for his pipe next to the pillow. Sister-in-law Shuangxi grumbled, complaining that he was getting up too late. She nagged at him without cease. He smoked a few bowls of tobacco, looked at the white light showing through the window paper, and got off the kang. After groping around on the east wall of the kitchen, he finally found the fishing net that Sister-in-law Shuangxi had just repaired yesterday.

The sparse stars were still shining in the sky. The alley was dark. Far away, the electric light at the Weixin Road intersection was dim and unclear, as if its color had been drained by the cold wind. He shivered, stepped on the frozen mud road, and hurried away. The firelight in the pipe bowl occasionally flashed a part of his face. It was filthy and greasy, as if he had never washed his face from birth until now. He was covered in fishy stench, and his hands and feet smelled of fish brine.

Walking onto Weixin Road, he left the darkness behind. The coachman sat huddled in the front seat of the carriage, dozing. The horse stood firmly on all four hooves, chewing its "liu zi" with its back to the wind. At the intersection with Zhongshan Road, the traffic police officer was pacing back and forth in the street. Shuangxi's spirits lifted as he walked, as if a cat was grabbing at his ears. He whistled and went straight to the East Wharf. The lead weights on the fishing net *ba-la ba-la* sounds.

The wind and waves constantly crashed in from the sea.

Far away, the British warship was flashing star-like lights. The waves roared, the sound of the fishermen's oars, and the people and lights on the dock were mixed together, creating a loud commotion. Brother Shuangxi became more and more anxious as he walked. He thought:

—Jiang Sheng must be getting angry waiting?

When he walked behind the Donghai Hotel, a sailor came from the south, with a woman. He was used to seeing this. He knew they were British sailors and White Russian dancers. The woman was laughing. The sailor seemed to have lost his footing, staggering towards Brother Shuangxi. A wave of overwhelming alcohol odor entered Brother Shuangxi's nostrils from the sailor.

The sailor suddenly pounced on Brother Shuangxi like a lion, grabbing him and hitting him. At first, Brother Shuangxi didn't dare to resist and kept dodging backwards, but the sailor was acting as if he had met an enemy, hitting him relentlessly. Brother Shuangxi, unable to bear it any longer, pushed the sailor with all his strength. The sailor fell into the small drainage ditch by the side of the road with a *pu-chi* sound. He was shouting wildly. The woman laughed and walked away alone.

The sailor was screaming and shouting, unable to get up. His body was splattered with muddy water. Seeing that things were going badly, Brother Shuangxi ran away. The police whistle sounded sharply behind him. As he ran near the bathhouse, he was caught by the patrolling police chief:

"Why are you running?"

"I…I'm in a hurry to go fishing…"

"Why is there blood on your face? Tell me the truth, what did you do?"

The police came up with the sailor.

"It was him—" pointing at Brother Shuangxi—"he robbed this foreigner!"

Brother Shuangxi was surrounded by terror, his whole body shivering, his lips trembling:

"He hit me for no reason, am I not allowed to fight back?"

The police chief slapped Brother Shuangxi hard across the face:

"Hit you? Why would an Englishman hit you!"

"Search him, see what he robbed?"

"First, take him to the station and we'll talk."

The sailor was sent to Weihai Hospital by the police chief in a horse-drawn carriage.

Brother Shuangxi was tied with ropes and dragged to the Public Security Bureau.

The storm raged more furiously. The snow on Liugong Island reflected the frozen clouds in the sky, white and vast. Far in the east, a ball of red light appeared on the horizon. The sun was about to rise. The great British warship stood tall on the sea, spewing thick smoke. The pier was filled with fishmongers, watching the returning fishing boats from afar. (The End)

Shen Bao This City Supplement

Talk

Abyssinia's Last Resistance 225

— Meng Ruo

Under the oppression of power, Abyssinia used flesh and blood to resist Italy's guns and bullets, fighting bitterly for seven months. Although the Abyssinian army has suffered repeated heavy blows, the Abyssinian people have not succumbed. Diplomatically, Abyssinia, in the League of Nations, firmly rejected the harsh conditions proposed by Italy and demanded that all sanctions stipulated in Article 16 of the League Covenant be fully implemented. Militarily, the Abyssinian army is preparing for a final resistance. The other day, crowds gathered at the racecourse in the Abyssinian capital, quietly listening to the Abyssinian king's edict, ordering men capable of wielding weapons to gather military equipment, bullets, and food, awaiting orders to depart. At that time, five thousand people immediately announced their willingness to fight to the death. Meanwhile, Abyssinian women continue to advise men to resist the Italian army with all their strength. The Abyssinian government has also issued a declaration, encouraging the people, saying that it is better to die as an Abyssinian ghost than to live as an Italian slave. The nation's determination to fight the enemy together is evident.

How Abyssinia's final resistance will turn out in the future cannot be determined now. Judging from the situation of the war, the future is more likely to be ominous than auspicious. However, we believe that if the Abyssinian army wins the battle, its morale will be boosted, and it is not absolutely hopeless to continue the struggle in the future and recover the lost land. Unfortunately, defeat is also glorious. The liberation struggle of oppressed peoples is inherently difficult. How could Abyssinia not understand that its own strength is weak and cannot withstand the blow of Italy's elite weapons? However, in order to fight for the oppressed peoples, they disregard everything and only resist to the death. Abyssinia's action both teaches the aggressor nation a lesson and encourages the oppressed peoples. We believe that in the future, if a group of ambitious people recklessly and blindly invade the weak, they will inevitably encounter strong resistance. Many people have discussed Abyssinia's resistance against the enemy, saying that it is brave, but unfortunately too unrealistic, resulting in today's tragic defeat. We think this is wrong. It must be known that Italy's attempt to annex Abyssinia is very ambitious. If Abyssinia does not dare to resist and submits, it would probably have already become a slave of Italy.

The East African War has reached a critical juncture. Abyssinia's last resistance is not only related to the survival of a country but also sufficient to determine the fate of oppressed peoples around the world.

Escape 226

— Yan

In winter, the northwest wind blew the bare branches, whistling. No one knows where the stray dogs have fled to. Occasionally, the sound of the night watchman floats from afar, making the countryside night more desolate and terrifying. Villagers are especially calculating. After eating dinner, they blew out the fire and huddled into broken cotton batting. They are reluctant to put more cooking oil in their dishes, and how attentive they are to the oil in their oil lamps!

The sky had no stars and no moon. The entire countryside lay quietly in the embrace of darkness, like a wounded jackal. However, Ah Gou in Donggou was suffering from a serious illness. His mother and daughter were waiting by his bedside. The oil lamp on the wall was still flickering with a ray of pale green light. The patient opened his mouth wide, his eyes rolled back, slightly yawning, looking like he was asleep or like he was dead. The mother and daughter's eyes were swollen and red like walnuts. They were worried about Ah Gou's illness and even more afraid of the tragedy that would come tomorrow morning. They hugged each other tightly, but the dilapidated house was attacked by arrow-like cold winds from all sides. They looked at Ah Gou's pale face and then paid attention to each other, as if exchanging the pain in their hearts.

The sound of the clapper floated from afar again. It was three o'clock in the morning. Dawn was just around the corner. The daughter finally snuggled against her mother's cold cheek, and said slowly, "Mom, let's listen to Dad and escape before dawn."

The mother instinctively hugged her daughter tighter. Tears flowed from everyone's eyes, dripping from the corners of their eyes along their cheeks, indistinguishable from which person they belonged. She breathed a sigh of relief from the depths of her heart, "But, Yuexiang, how can Dad escape when he is ill?"

She was immediately afraid of waking up Ah Gou on the bed, so she moved from one end of the bed to the other, but Ah Gou was still sleeping like he was dead. She wiped her tears with the corner of her clothes and continued:

"There really aren't any good people in this world! That little devil, Afu, used to receive so many benefits from your dad, but now he has stumbled into a good fortune and become a rent collector. His eyes are growing out of his forehead and he won't sell anyone any favors…" She sobbed and couldn't continue. Afu's dog face seemed to be standing in front of her:

"Hmph! If you don't pay your rent, what am I, Afu, supposed to eat! To put it bluntly, Yuexiang is so old, it would be a disgrace to you to become a concubine for Master Hu! I will pick her up tomorrow by small sedan. Old man, you better think about it clearly!"

He pushed Ah Gou, and swaying, left. Ah Gou had been sick for more than two months. When Afu came to the door today, he barely straightened his back from the bed and said many good words, but he was already out of breath. Without warning, Afu pushed him in the chest, and he rolled down from the edge of the bed, speechless for a long time. There was only a trace of breath rising and falling in his chest.

The mother and daughter scrambled, heated a towel, and used the folk method of pricking the soles of his feet. When Ah Gou woke up, he mustered all his strength to slap his old wife, shouting, "You heartless pig and dog!" But he immediately understood that the pig and dog had already run back to the city to fawn over Master Hu. He watched his wife stroking her slapped cheek, and he said apologetically:

"I said long ago that guarding these few acres of land will eventually lead to starvation! You listen to me and escape! I am not…useful…anymore!"

The mother and daughter lay on the edge of the bed, crying. Ah Gou gnashed his teeth in hatred.

Now the firelight on the wall was even smaller and flickering, about to go out. The mother could only shed tears and sigh. She couldn't abandon her sick husband and escape, and she didn't want to give her own flesh and blood to those dog things.

Ah Gou suddenly woke up, and he still shouted loudly, "Escape! What's the point of guarding me!" He tried hard to struggle up from the bed, but his hands went limp, and he fell from the corner of the bed like a piece of luggage, his mouth stained with a stream of red blood—he was dead.

The wife threw herself on the corpse, crying and shouting…

The daughter suddenly shouted as if waking up from a dream, "Mom, escape!" Like her father's voice, it was powerful, "What's the point of guarding me!"

"But what about your dad?" The mother wanted to pick up Ah Gou's corpse.

"The living can't wait for the dead!" She was frantically packing things, not knowing where the strength came from, and pulled her mother away.

The sky was slowly brightening, and raindrops were floating in the air. They stepped on the muddy road and left the village, but the distance was a fog…
